when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她確實做了一些事 , 但真正的目的是要說未來會比這個還多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 再次發明電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , 巴貝奇的機器完全是機械化的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論上的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是從數學的角度來的 , 但turing告訴我們一些非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你如何製造電腦 , 都不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論是你的電腦的機械裝置 , 像是babbage的裝置 , 或是像現今的電子裝置 , 或是未來的細胞 , 或者 , 細胞 , 或者 , 一旦我們進入奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 。 這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上是計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這就是所謂的教會論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你看到了這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage其實是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們現今用電腦所做的事 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓各位了解它有多慢 , 它有大約1k的記憶力 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用的是打孔卡 , 被餵進去 , 跑的速度大約是一萬倍 , 第一個zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一包鐵包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想的話 , 你可以加上額外的記憶力 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案中 , 有數以百計的計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫的 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個計畫就是我們稱之為 「 計劃28 」 , 這也是我以doronswaade為起始的一個慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的運算策展人 , 也是開這個計劃來建造不同引擎的人 , 我們的計劃是要建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓這裡 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有很多部件 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一個是巴貝奇的檔案掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是計算機模擬這台機器 , 最後一部分是要在科學博物館實體建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為你面前有一片小晶片 , 你必須看一下這個神奇的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作 。 我可能聞它 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫信 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎就存在 , 就一定會引導未來的科學軌跡 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造它 , 因為他總是在想新的計畫 , 但當它真的被建造出來時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我給你一點點的味道 , 看看它在動作時的樣子 , 影片中顯示了cpu機制的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組cogs , 它會加上 。 這是加入的機制 , 所以你想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們就有了 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像填滿的演講中 , 雅恩•亞瑟•亞伯蘭展示了他最近三項關於人性的計畫 , 我們的棲息地拍攝了他的一系列 「 天文照片 」 , 來自世界各地的個人訪談 , 來自他網路上的 「 六十億人 」 , 他很快就放棄了電影 , 「 家 」 , 透過呼吸影片來記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅諾•亞瑟•亞伯特蘭在寬廣的角度捕捉到脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 以飛機來到這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中釋放出九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談到生態學 , 一年內我把二氧化碳當成法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回家時 , 我得要殺一位法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須以另一種方式來做我的碳排卵 , 就像我每次都要做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作就是展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些我去年拍的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	阿爾伯塔沙油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你們知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的事 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯達人的工作非op24小時 , 七小時以上 , 盡可能多提取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量比每年多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克萊尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	珊瑚的百分之百可能在2050年前就消失了 , 因為全球暖化 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋生物多樣性的重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 。 去年夏天我拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前 , 這張照片是不可能做到的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	在大西洋和太平洋之間 , 有一種新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	自從1960年起 , 北極的厚度下降了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	沒有冰的kilimanjaro有新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了百分之八十的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家的說法 , 在一百年內 , 所有的山冰都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命很重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像艾爾•高爾說的 , 二十億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河裡 。
return of fish men .	回到漁人身上 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類依賴魚類生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今 , 70%的魚類過度開發 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao , 如果我們不改變我們的捕魚系統 , 2050年就會消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	美麗的照片 , 在非洲 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	六個人中的一個人不夠吃東西 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人不夠吃東西 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米是許多地方的主要食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 百分之九十的玉米被用來餵養動物或做石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅 , 棕櫚樹種植 。
every year we lose 50 thousand square miles in deforestation .	每年我們損失了五萬平方英里的森林砍伐 。

i always show my pictures in the street .	我總是在街上展示我的照片 。

12th man: if i was to go back to iraq and speak to the people , i'd have to bow down and kiss their feet .	第十二個男人:如果我回到伊拉克 , 和人民說話 , 我就得向下吹 , 親吻他們的腳 。
just as that woman tried to kiss my feet when we were taking her sons .	正如那位女士試著親吻我腳時 , 我們要照顧她的兒子 。
and i feel humbled by their strength .	我對他們的力量感到謙卑 。
and i will forever feel a need to make reparations to iraq .	我永遠感覺到 , 需要對伊拉克做出回應 。

at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	目前 , 我的家人非常貧窮 , 我在深圳的人生 , 只是為了證明我能賺更多錢 , 讓我的父母能繼續生活 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經有四十五億年了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 已經有數億年前了 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類已經直立行走了20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們成功地適應整個星球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數世代以來 , 我們都在養育我們的孩子 , 不像其他數百萬種住在我們旁邊的物種 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我親眼目睹地球和它在天空中高高處的居民 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的幸福有關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚 , 繁殖 , 農業仍然是世界上最先進的人類佔領 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起 , 遠遠比我們分裂的東西還要多 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的天賦有同樣的需求 , 希望能超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們在養育牆壁上留住我們 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天 , 我們最大的戰役是要保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們已經徹底地改變了它 , 遠超過人類歷史上的所有歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界一半的森林消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危及自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們的速度比地球能維持的速度還要快很多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道解決方案現今是可行的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這個趨勢 , 讓它更好 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德.雷尼克的演講顯示 , 將來將健康照護的低價和快速基因序列調低 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 健康照護 , 科學 , 科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命中 , 歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體的複製品 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 那個y的小複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是個小東西 , 讓你不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 你會看到這個雙螺旋結構 , 生命的密碼和這四個生物化學信件的密碼 , 或我們稱之為基礎:a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以投擲大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我要在這個1280年到800次的解析度螢幕上放一個鹼基 , 我們需要3 , 000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便一提 , y染色體決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	實際上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美金後 , 基因組被排序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後一個版本被刊出 , 他們持續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都在一個像這樣的機器上完成 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個基地都要花一塊錢 , 一個非常慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴你們 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們把基因組做成50份複製品 , 我們把這些複製品做成50頁然後我們將它們定序 , 大規模平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它帶到軟體中 , 我們重新組合它 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給各位看這張圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gbass , 對吧 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台在其中一台機器上運行:一週內有200個gbabases 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天 , 這兩百人將改變到六百人 , 這步調沒有減速的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 根據基礎定序的價格下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這相當於你在1998年用氣體填滿車子 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星和後面兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點、所有醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、舊的定序方式 , 還有新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是物流尺度 , 通常你不會看到這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全球人類基因組定序的能力是今年大約五萬到十萬的人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道這個基於被安置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預期會增加兩倍、三倍或四倍 , 年復一年 , 才能預見到可預見的未來 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別有一間實驗室 , 代表所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做北京基因組學院 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國人對新的月球贏得了這個比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她展示了第二階段的雌激素接收乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和輻射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著三個卵巢癌復發 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時 , 患有更多卵巢癌、更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性骨髓性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後就死了 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這個女人被治療的方式 , 在短短的10年內 , 看起來會像血液一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	因為像我的同事 , 瑞克.威爾森 , 在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 她決定看看這位女士後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他的基因序列 , 皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚和癌症骨髓 , 在幾週內 , 他定序了兩者的基因組 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他把這兩組基因組拿來做軟體比較 , 他發現 , 在其他東西中 , 是一個耗損 , 一個兩千多億個鹼基 , 一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有突變 , 你就有90%的可能性在你的生命中得到癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這並沒有幫助這位女士 , 但如果你願意的話 , 它的確有嚴重的、深刻的影響她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因測試 , 然後他們明白了 , 那麼他們就可以定期篩檢 , 他們可以早期發現癌症 , 甚至可能活得更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向你們介紹啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是個非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀和一些英雄的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的就是分離性dstonia 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了dopa , 他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但他們並沒有完全不符合症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片裡的先生叫joebeery他很幸運能成為一家叫做生命科技的公司
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是兩家公司之一 , 製造出大量的基因定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他所做的是讓他的孩子順序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 一系列突變發生在一個叫做spr的基因中 , 這對產生血清素的產生負責 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在左上角 , 他們給了這些孩子一個血清素的先驅藥 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有完整的基因定序 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 成本是10萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	一年後 , 要花100美元 , 或花一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有小小的尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克出現在兒童醫院裡 , 帶著這種不良的肚子 , 就像一個飢荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西時 , 他的腸道基本上會打開 , 排泄物進入他的腸道 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百多次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 拜託我 , 我很痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓我們把這個孩子的基因序列拿出來 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現一個基因突變 , 負責控制細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	理論是 , 他對食物的生理反應有一些免疫反應 , 基本上 , 這是自然的反應 , 造成了一些編寫細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但那些調節下來的基因已經破壞了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也提供了骨髓移植的治療 , 他接受了這個治療 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的可怕康復之後 , 他現在正在吃一口沙發 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	用基因組作為普遍診斷的前景 , 現今就在我們身上 。

so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植玉米、小麥、大豆和其他農作物 , 它們非常包容乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得要繼續成長、吃基因改造食物 , 而這也是我今天唯一能採取的職位 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫特展示了他的骨髓採礦器 , 它能很快地把骨髓和捐贈者保存下來 。 他強調 , 骨髓中的成人幹細胞能被用來治療許多終端條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 以拯救白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 將軍麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一位來自我身上的醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌子上 , 我們用這種小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法基本上就是把這個放到軟組織中 , 把它插入硬骨頭 , 進入tuchus , 每次用針筒來啟動大約十磅的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把它送到護士面前 , 她將它放進一個tin 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 , 我們一而再再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常有兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	最後 , 我的手臂是索索爾 , 我手上有個通話 , 更不用說bob , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 像是瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道 , 這種手術在40年內並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個極小入侵的方法 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦工 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式在這裡顯示 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準來看待病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭幾十次 , 我們只進入骨頭 , 進入髖骨的前面 , 或髖骨的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、強大的導管 , 帶著特殊的電線路尖 , 留在粗糙的骨髓中 , 跟著骨髓的輪廓 , 當它移動時 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以 , 它能讓你非常迅速地吸出骨髓 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以做多次通過同樣的入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , 鮑勃就能拿到刺穿 , 當地麻醉 , 做這個收穫是門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小小的補助金 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最終我們得到了兩個大型動物和豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們驚訝地發現 , 我們不只把骨髓拿出來 , 還得到了骨髓內的幹細胞活動的10倍 , 與一般裝置相比 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置是去年fda核准的 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是活體病人 , 你可以看到它跟著靈活的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人身上 , 會有兩條路 , 同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地的麻醉劑下完成的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞比同一個病人的標準方法要多三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的身體中 , 包括骨髓中的血液幹細胞 , 我們用這種方式來當幹細胞療法 , 已經超過40年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人的其他疾病 , 比如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至神經學 , 來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出櫃 , 我們正在商業化 , 今年 , 第2.0名骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能讓更多幹細胞被翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人簽署 , 成為潛在救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可以讓你在未來更年輕、更健康時 , 去銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 去使用在未來你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這是我們骨髓移植者的照片 , 每年在史丹佛 , 她們會聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和弗雷特•蓋瑞特•萊西提出了一個有爭議性的宇宙模型 , 可能可以回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它是你所見過最美麗的8d立體粒子和力量的模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、技術、物理、物理、科學、科學、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlitlisi理論上所有事物的理論
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 , 甜蜜 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘 , 我要盡我所能去描述粒子物理的美麗 , 沒有方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚都有上千個珊瑚蟲 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚合物不斷地分裂成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級智慧的珊瑚 , 我們可以一個人 , 然後問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點 , 與他的鄰居相比 , 如果只是機會 , 或命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們把溫度調高過後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題是完全愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是很有意義的 , 你看 , 我有衝浪來證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚合劑會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居是非常相似的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在所有其他的地點 , 但經驗卻是不同的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 超級智慧的珊瑚 , 會特別準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常精確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪最初是由薛丁格和他的貓所描述的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設置中 , 薛丁格在一個放射性樣本中 , 由量子力學的定律 , 分成一個放射性狀態 , 而不是放射性狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本中 , 樣本會放射 , 它會引發一種觸發 , 釋放毒藥和薛丁格會死 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個人都有不同的經驗 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	無論如何 , 另一個都不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說是很怪的 , 因為我們每個人都只體驗到個人存在 , 我們也看不到其他分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	彷彿我們每一個人 , 像這裡的薛丁格 , 有點像是珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這個世界是怎麼運作的
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用一個句子來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都可以 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切都發生了 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都歸功於幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我要描述我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼 , 以及平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 一道質子和反質子的束縛會加速到接近光速 , 並聚集在一起 , 產生出一股純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子 , 用探測器和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器──在日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有17英哩的圓圈 , 當它在運作時 , 比蒙特利市的電力高出五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確地預測任何個體碰撞中產生的粒子 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都被實現 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理告訴我們哪些粒子可以產生 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質子和能量必須和質子和反質子相同 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子的質量都比這個能量限度更大 , 對我們來說仍然是隱形的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器這麼令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越前所未有的能量限制七倍 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 讓我來描述我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一大堆亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這個房間裡的很多人都做得很好 , 把他們推過來 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中立的夥伴 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷 , 和非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上方的夸克有很大的質量 , 三的結合 , 使質子和中子在原子中形成 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左右和右邊的品種中 , 有抗粒子伴侶攜帶著相反的載荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉第二代和第三代 , 相同的載荷和第一代相同 , 但有更高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都和不同力量粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力透過光子的粒子 , 與電荷相互作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種很弱的力量 , 叫做 , 相當不想像 , 較弱的力量 , 只與左撇子物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶有不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 以三種不同品種:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann--他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 引力的作用 , 透過質量和旋轉來與物質產生作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每種力都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力與物質相互作用 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的對應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個尚未被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它會給予所有其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的奧秘是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一個美麗的可能性 , 來結束這場演說 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來算出這些不同的粒子 , 會有226個粒子 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	這是很多粒子用來追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然會有這麼多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案會浮現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克三分之一有電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個夸克和一個下夸克結合成質子時 , 它就有一連串的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷實際上是另外兩個載荷的組合:超電荷和弱電荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開來 , 在這二維載荷空間中 , 電荷是這些粒子位置沿著垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會根據超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這就是所謂的 「 聯合電路 」 模型 , 它在1967年被放回來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大多數人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯有大量的質量 , 打破了這個斜率模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它使弱力變得非常弱 , 使得弱粒子變弱 , 大量質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯坐落在這個圖表中的水平方向 , 電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量 , 與電荷垂直方向的電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被二維空間中的粒子載荷所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力推向它的兩個載荷方向 , 並在這些方向繪製出夸克力粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維空間中定位 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用 , 自然就會讓物體保持完美的平衡 , 沿著這四個載荷方向 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一顆粒子和反粒子碰撞 , 它會產生一股能量 , 以及四個載荷方向的總載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時此刻 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要它擁有相同的能量 , 且能維持完全的載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 指控必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可能會衰退成一個電子和一個中子 , 這三個粒子仍然是零的載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式並不只是很漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們哪些互動是可以發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四維空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強相互作用 , 它有很棒的六角形對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的交互作用中 , 強力粒子 , 比如這個 , 和有色的夸克交互作用 , 比如這個綠色的夸克 , 給夸克一個不同的顏色載荷這個紅色的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的交互作用每秒發生數百萬次在我們身體的每個原子中 , 將原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應三種力並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也可以再加上兩個載荷與重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們包起來 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們全部都分開 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看到它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這種模式符合了我們目前對於大自然如何在這些基本粒子所建立的最佳知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是極限的 , 是我們能在實驗中找到的 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙的運作方式非常美麗 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要談談一些關於我們尚未知的新古老想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把手伸到全芝加拉達上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有組成宇宙的粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測新的粒子 , 讓實驗達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中產生 , 和希格斯粒子如何突破電磁化的模式 , 來產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引進新的力量 , 引進新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子在這個方向上有哪些載荷 , 然後我們可以把它轉向另一個方向 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	假如我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以建立標準載荷 , 以六度載荷的形式 , 來作為這更完美的七度載荷空間的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 帕蒂和薩姆在1973年引入了一項大型統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些差異 , 粒子看起來似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包含以子組成的模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測那些從未被看見的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新的力量粒子的存在 , 該作用很像弱力 , 只是弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七維空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 並考慮一個關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:第二代和第三代物質在六維載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷空間 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨一無二的被六個載荷辨識出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們就可以把獨特的載荷給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整體的圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二代、第三代物質 , 與第一代相關 , 是由所謂的 「 審判 」 的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種八度空間的載荷模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外謊言集團e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的曲線形狀 , 有248個維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	每一個點都與這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀相對應 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時期 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學結合 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀可以描述宇宙在最小的尺度運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的模式是活在八度載荷空間中 , 非常美麗 , 它總結成千上萬個可能的粒子間的互動 , 每一個都只是這種複雜形狀的表面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	隨著我們旋轉 , 我們可以看到其中許多複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們就能在八度空間中觀察這個模式 , 同時看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何一個單一物件 , 我們可以看到一些新粒子被這個圖案所需要的孔洞 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	那裡有20個空隙 , 新粒子應該有二個被巴黎粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們的位置來看 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子那樣的尺寸 , 但它們有色荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成了這個模式 , 給我們全e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有非常深的數學根 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大數學美麗的物體能夠描述粒子相互作用的真相 , 以最小規模的想像力描述 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然被數學所描述的這個想法完全不是新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的偉大書 , 不斷地對我們的目光開放 , 以數學的語言寫 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形 , 圓形和其他幾何形狀 , 沒有這些形狀是人類無法理解的 ; 沒有這些 , 一個在黑暗的迷宮中漫遊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著追蹤伽利略的指導 , 用三角形、圓形和其他幾何形狀來描述粒子物理的數學 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我研究這個東西時 , 數學可以和黑暗迷宮相似 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這張數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何圖形 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這個數學將我們的宇宙描述為一個生長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在所有可能的位置相互作用 , 根據一個美麗的模式 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著越來越多的圖案使用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們也許能看到大自然是否使用這個e8圖案或另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是一場很棒的冒險旅程 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那會非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但對這個e8理論不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 差不多 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這種理論和其他類似的理論是很長的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多辛苦的工作 , 知道這些想法可能最終不會實現大自然 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的樣子:有很多野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	和任何大型投資一樣 , 要放棄一行不通的研究方式 , 情緒上是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學中 , 如果事情不成功 , 你得要把它弄出來 , 嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	要保持清潔和幸福的唯一方法 , 就是保持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡我所能地過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生活 , 物理、愛和衝浪我自己的三項載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我研究的物理成分都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年 , 我住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是我父母最大的謎團之一 , 我如何能在沒有全職工作的情況下生存下來 , 生存下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊家辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的觀點是相似的 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個非常不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心租金讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時 , 過著遊牧的存在很艱難 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 在我的生活中保持平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我能花很多時間和超級智慧珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興被邀請來到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概了解了百分之二 , 但我還是很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的所有東西的理論:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 。 原因有少數人感到興奮 , 因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你說我們應該想一下宇宙 , 心臟裡最小的東西 , 可能是e8的可能性嗎 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度 , 還是......
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在我給你們看的圖案 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理學有關 , 已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我所說的我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 和它如何融入e8模式 , 可能是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 實際上代表著這個高維度物體的對稱性 , 會在我們體驗的時空中扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們所看到的這些基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論家 , 如我所知 , 用較小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何把電子和e8有關 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	諾曼:不 , 這會是e8形狀的對稱性 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 隨著形狀在時空移動 , 它在扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它的方向是粒子的形狀 。 克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它比較大嗎 ? 比較小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	諾曼:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子是指點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西是可以同時擴展和發展的 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用珊瑚的比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8進來的形狀就是每一次都附著在時空的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的 , 形狀的扭曲了方向 , 形狀在移動時扭曲了曲面 , 就是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 他們表現出自己是指點 , 並以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能否更清楚一點 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我肯定想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	非常謝謝你們來了 。 這真的很吸引人 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍.古拉爾談到塔瑞和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助在波動的非洲小鎮居住 , 和威脅動物的威脅 。
