it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是國家的安全對其士兵和國防部而言 , 不再是問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它是鎖定其制度的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你們一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直的階級制度 , 專業任務 , 指揮結構完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商業界你知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	你的網絡能力很重要 , 包括在你的政府和外在 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是阿什丹的第三法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 不要問我 「 崩解 」 的第一個法律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明這些法律 ; 如果有第三條法律的話 , 聽起來比較好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三條法則是 , 在現代的時代 , 一切都和一切有關 , 最重要的事是你能做的 , 就是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的一點是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊註冊 , 不論你是企業 , 你的間接點 , 你和他人建立網路的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白這一點 , 在工業上 , 政府不是 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事情 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 各位先生女士 , 我們現在被困在一種以前從來沒有相同的情況下 , 那也是我們彼此共同的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主導我們 , 作為國家安全的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的盟友 , 像是納多 , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	現在不再是這樣了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互關聯和大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和敵人分享了命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我是外交官 , 在1970年代 , 我和日內瓦的蘇聯協定談判 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩方都知道 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人共享命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的大障礙之一是以色列 , 我認為巴勒斯坦人並不了解他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 女士們先生們 , 過去的願景和詩人提出 , 我們必須認真看待公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首詩為結尾 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐妮的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 送給鐘聲的誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是島嶼 。 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	內容是: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 因為我參與的人 , 不要去問鐘聲 , 要為你賺錢 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對於約翰•唐納 , 道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 我們生存的方程式之一 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽、健康、丹•布雷特納和團隊 , 研究世界的 「 藍色區 」 , 他們的長者和vim一起生活 , 在tedxtc記錄年齡 。 他分享了九項常見的飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們能在一百歲時流產 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、科學、科學、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到100+ ?
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎研究指出 , 在某些生物限制下 , 平均人的壽命只有百分之十 , 是由我們的基因來決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是由我們的生活方式所主宰 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能想出一個真正的公式來長壽 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般的美國人長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們 ,
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正能讓我們活得更好的事物 , 有很多疑惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補給品時 , 你應該拿它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼這些荷爾蒙又或者逆流呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	是否有目的呢 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理研究所合作 , 國家老化研究所 , 找出四個人口統計的地區 , 地理學定義的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 帶一組專家到那裡 , 來調查這些人的行為 , 來調查跨文化的陳述 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後 , 我要告訴你們那段陳述是甚麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先 , 我想要破除一些常見的迷思 , 談到長壽 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很努力 , 你就能活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國大約有五千人當中只有一人活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機率很低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使在美國 , 人口成長最快 , 還是很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是為了長壽而編寫的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們為所謂的 「 繁榮成功 」 計畫 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 繁衍成功 」 , 意思是 「 你有孩子的年齡 」 , 接著是 「 下一代 」 , 「 孩子的年齡 」 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後 , 演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人 , 在兩者之間 , 則是相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要做到一百歲 , 你不僅要有很好的生活方式 , 你還得贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以減緩、逆轉 , 甚至阻止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 我們有99件事情可以讓我們變老 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們就不會回來了 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太硬 , 在膝蓋上 , 磨損軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用白斑連結起來 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 用的是t 。 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年一次就轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每次他們轉到那裡 , 就會有一些損害 , 造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它以指數型的方式成長 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像是當我們有披頭四的專輯或老鷹的專輯時 , 我們會在錄音帶上複製 , 讓朋友們複製錄錄錄錄錄音帶 , 很快地 , 錄音帶的成功世代聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化速度比一個12歲的人快了125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果你沒有辦法減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約是90年 , 對女人來說 , 再多一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家 , 平均壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	在這條線上 , 我們離開了大約12年的美好時光 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們都可以做到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 長期疾病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 , 絕大部分時間都不會有慢性病、心臟病、癌症、糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要消失這些年齡最好的方法就是去看世界各地的文化 , 實際上正在經歷他們的文化 , 那裡的人比我們年齡100歲 , 比我們多出十倍 , 預期壽命是十幾年 , 中年的死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸找到第一條藍色區大約有125英里 , 在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做nuoro省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有這個區域 , 男人的壽命最長 , 大約比美國這裡的百歲人多十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只達到100歲 , 他們還用非凡的vigor來做這件事 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 102歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 蕭條木 , 打敗比他們年輕60歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史回溯到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它其實是一個被隔離的銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這塊土地很不具侵蝕性 , 大多是牧羊人 , 偶爾 , 較弱的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎 , 以它們能帶進田野的食物為中心 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一堆未發酵的小麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂麵包 , 由草食動物製成的一種乳酪 , 乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸中很高 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米餵養的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何葡萄酒都要高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密在於他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會中最重要的元素之一就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 你得到的越多平等 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 而不是看到運動畫面上的游泳日曆 , 你看到月曆的百歲人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不僅對你的老父母親有好處 , 要讓他們和家人親近 , 預期壽命約四到六年的研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子而言 , 死亡率也比較低 , 疾病的比率也比較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了第二個藍色區塊 , 位於東京南部大約800英里 , 位於okinawa的阿奇拉群島 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的零地 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是一個最古老的女性族群被發現的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在那裡 , 人們有世界上最長的殘疾壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活了很久 , 通常會在牠們的睡眠中死亡 , 很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性愛之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命比美國人多了七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	我們在美國有五倍的百歲人 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	美國有五分之一的殖民地和乳癌 , 大型殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的前六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化已經證實了這些數字 , 表示他們有強烈的教導力 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面有許多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	美國人吃大約八倍的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免過量 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:牠們吃掉較小的盤子 , 所以牠們通常在每一隻坐下的熱量都比較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 在談話時 , 你可以無心地吃東西 , 他們在櫃台上 , 把食物拿走 , 然後把它送到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有3000歲的年紀 , 我認為這是史上最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混合物所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 哈拉 , 哈特 , 哈特 , 飲食 。 」
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯之前說 , 要提醒他們不要再吃東西 , 因為他們的胃是80% 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花上半小時才能從肚子傳到大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住 , 要在80%停止 , 它能協助你避免做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞一樣 , okinawa有一些社會結構 , 我們可以把長壽聯結在一起 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道隔離會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	15年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經下降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運 , 生在okinawa , 你就生在一個系統裡 , 你自動自動就有一半的朋友陪伴你人生 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為moai 。 如果你在moai中 , 你被期待要分享這個機會 , 如果你幸運的話 , 孩子生病了 , 父母死了 , 你總是會有一個有你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這位特殊的moai女士 , 這五位女士已經在一起了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人的生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著退休給簡單的椅子 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語中 , 甚至沒有退休的詞語 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 整個人生都會有一個字 , 這個字是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約翻譯了 , 意思是 「 你早上醒來的原因 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位102歲的karatester來說 , 他的ikigai正攜帶著這件軍事藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位百歲的漁夫來說 , 每週要捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所給了我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們是非常文化上的直覺 , 那些提出了問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位102歲的老婦人而言 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩在101年半之間分開 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 是什麼樣的感覺 , 可以保持一個曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回頭說: 「 感覺就像跳入天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我的地理編輯希望我找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們研究明尼蘇達的草原 , 那裡其實有很高比例的百歲人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再轉向數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口 , 在加州的第七天冒險家中 , 都集中在洛馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	先進主義者是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日落慶祝他們的休息日 , 星期五日落 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個 「 時間24小時的庇護所 」 , 他們稱之為 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	相較之下 , 他們遵循了五個小習慣 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是八十歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對於一位先進主義的女性來說 , 他們的平均壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	不同之處在於男性之間 , 比美國人多出11年的預期壽命 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 我認為它最能說明這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異性戀的社群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白色、黑色、西班牙裔、亞洲 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 他們大部分時間都遵循著儀式的生活 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經取得飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:第一章 , 詩句是29種 。 上帝談到傳承和種子 , 再談談綠色植物 , 顯然缺少的是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子們需要開車 , 他們會停止一切 , 專注在神、社交網路上 , 然後 , 在宗教中 , 天生會走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	它的力量並不是偶爾完成的 , 它的力量是每週都完成一次 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有任何一個很難 。 沒有一個花費 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向和其他冒險家在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一場冒險家派對 , 你不會看到有人在搖吉姆姆姆姆光燈或捲起一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談論他們的下一個自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻且可測量的方式互相影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化讓埃爾斯•沃爾斯•沃爾斯•沃爾斯感到羞恥 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellswharem97歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是數百萬富翁 , 但當包商想要六千美元去建立隱私的圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了我自己做得到的那一筆錢 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以在接下來的三天裡 , 他出去打擊水泥 , 四處晃動 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可想而知 , 也許在第四天 , 他最後到達手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不像桌上的那個人 , 做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月仍然做了二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德.羅林斯 , 103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始了游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡戴上板子 , 扔出羅斯特尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這兩個城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從她的日子開始 , 帶著升重 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她走進她的根部 , 1994年的卡迪拉克賽維爾 , 撕下聖伯納多高速公路 , 在那裡 , 她仍然自願參與七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我去過19次艱難的探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是你遇見唯一一個騎腳踏車的人 , 穿越撒哈拉沙漠 , 沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有冒險 , 比起在華盛頓特區開槍更駭人 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中的共通點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的事是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功歸結為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經做過兩次藍色藍色的探險 , 這些共同的探險人員確實是如此 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要說出一個喜劇 , 沒有一個運動 , 至少我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 這樣他們不斷地被推進實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的okinawan女性站在地上 , 她們每天坐在地板上30到40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅行到商店 , 或教堂或朋友家 , 都會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕來推動花園工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒卡路里和跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做刻意的身體活動時 , 是他們喜歡的事 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一證實的方式就是脫離認知衰退 , 而他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式生活 , 所以他們有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間減少 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有祖先的調查 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在急促或緊張時 , 會觸發一種稱為 「 發炎反應 」 的現象 , 和阿茲海默症的一切有關 , 到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢15分鐘 , 你就會把發炎狀態轉變成更反炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們的字彙有目的、ikigai , 就像okinawanns一樣 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你人生中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的目的 , 他們活化了自己的人生 , 這價值約七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝點酒 , 而不是賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向於吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略可以避免過量 , 小東西在對的時間將它們推離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何連結的 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先把家人放第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和老化的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於信仰型的社區 , 值4到14年的預期壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就是活躍地圍繞著對的人 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗蘭罕研究得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友肥胖 , 會有50%的機率超重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人住在一起 , 隨著時間 , 會有很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友對於娛樂的概念是實體的活動 , 弓弦 , 或演奏曲棍球 , 腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但他們吃得不對 , 而且他們很投入 , 信任和值得信賴 , 這將會對時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 在歷史上 , 沒有飲食是超過2%的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常從一月開始 , 通常是十月份完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽時 , 藥丸或任何其他東西都沒有短期的固定方案 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最重要的事 , 多年以後 , 和你的生活 。 謝謝 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	那種導電力 ; 一扇窗從清晰轉換到開關的空白 ; 一顆製造音樂的水母 。 所有的東西都存在 。 卡塔琳娜•莫塔說:該是和它一起玩的時候了 。 莫塔帶領我們參觀驚喜且酷炫的新材料的旅程 , 建議我們找出它們的好處 , 去實驗、修補 , 並有樂趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩智能材料的遊戲 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一台車 , 這樣他才能運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起一輛車 , 同時也因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間 , 我們了解事情是如何運作的 , 以及如何做出來的 , 這樣我們就能建立並修復它們 , 或最少有資訊的決策 , 來決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀後半葉 , 許多的圓頂做法都已經消失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者和開放原始碼模型將這些知識帶入我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個階段 , 到構成的階段 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道傳統的材料 , 像是紙和紡織品的構成 , 以及它們如何生產 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些奇妙的、具體的複合材料塑膠 , 會改變形狀、會導電的顏料、會改變顏色的顏色、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	導電墨水讓我們繪製電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我拿的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造觸摸感測器 , 藉由打開這個小光來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家用的導電墨水 , 但近期的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能用雷射印表機和筆 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張是加上無色光驅光粒子的水晶 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般水晶只能在邊緣散射光線 , 這個光照在整個表面上 , 當我打開燈光時 , 會照亮整個表面 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這材料有兩種已知的應用 , 包括內部設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而溫室色素在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 溫度只比環境溫度稍高一點 , 你可以看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的其中一個原則是嬰兒瓶子裡的其他東西 , 所以當內容物夠酷的時候 , 它會指出 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常被稱為智慧材料的東西 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們將成為我們日常使用的物體和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛天車科幻小說給我們保證 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 根據溫度 , 按鍵板會滾起來 , 窗戶會在開關上變得不一樣 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天要談智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物如何運作 , 以及它們是如何製造的 , 也因為我相信我們應該更深入地了解構成我們世界的元件 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技合成的未來不夠了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用在如何使用它們 , 很少人會說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們主要存在於貿易秘密和專利領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 科斯泰男孩和我成立了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、出版資訊 , 鼓勵其他人在任何時候都能做出貢獻 , 集體資源 , 像是研究論文和教學 , 和其他像我們一樣的製造者 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個龐大、集體的資料庫 , 用智慧材料來發送自身資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要關心智慧材料有多有效 ? 它們是由什麼組成 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的事物 , 我們不了解和使用的東西最終會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、衣服、我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們生活在一個由智慧材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並理解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是由tinker推動 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家和改善者 , 從山腳踏車到半導體 , 個人電腦 , 飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家了解到這一點 , 當時他們發表了一篇論文 , 以更簡單的方式製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker在那時完全沒有化學經驗 , 直到那時為止 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的創作空間中進行實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具來進行實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至用他自己的蒸氣混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/maker的教練 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬丹後來在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括他嘗試過的東西 , 沒有用 , 其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	約旦的主要創新形式是把一個在大學的一個良好實驗室裡創造出來的實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重製它 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 來製造他自己 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以找到他離開的地方 , 甚至設計更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提一下她的專案計畫的目標 , 就是強調材料的表現特質 , 同時把焦點放在建造者的創意和技巧上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備非常強大 , 它們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但在設計中 , 限制了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來讓我們從預設的限制中解放出來 , 來教導我們材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有銅膠貼在mp3和磁鐵上 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他的製造者漢娜發表了她的食譜讓任何人複製和複製它們
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子產品是材料科學中最有希望的分支之一 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的工藝作品 , 她分享她的發現 , 打開了一連串新的可能性 , 兩者都很吸引人和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	製造者有趣的是 , 我們從熱情和好奇心中創造出來 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常用不尋常的角度來處理問題 , 在這個過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人實驗材料 , 研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正適合我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像是tednelson在1970年代初 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型主體 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人夢想要在家裡裝一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 我站在這裡有點奇怪 , 說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 對於新興科技的知識 , 最好的方式就是確保我們有對未來的說法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們進入了玻璃泡 , 關上門 , 按住加速器 , 依賴我們的眼睛 , 來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面的幾輛車子後面的車子 。 但如果車子能和彼此分享資料 , 關於他們的位置和速度 , 並使用模型來計算路上的每個人的安全路徑 ? 珍妮佛•哈利 , 想像一個沒有意外世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•海利:如果汽車能說話 , 意外可能會避免意外發生 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的一件事 , 但事實是 , 宗教偶像和好運迷人在世界各地出現在儀表板上 , 背叛了事實 , 我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國十六到十九歲人死亡的主要原因 , 這些事故中有百分之七十五的意外與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人能確定 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上是個年輕的司機 , 在我面前的車子裡 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不會慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在高速公路上停下來 , 停下來 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65到零 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abck很快就開始了 , 車子還沒停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋部署 , 車子很幸運 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子停止了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以透過讓車子彼此交談來改變駕駛的經驗 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們想想開車的經驗是什麼樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上你的車 , 關上門 , 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的工作任務是要在半球路徑下導航 , 在其他的金屬巨人當中 , 以超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只要指引你是你的雙眼 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的 , 不是為了這個任務而設計的眼睛 , 但人們會要求你做像這樣的事 , 你想要做車道改變 , 他們最先要求你做的事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從馬路上拿走 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 檢查你的盲點 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的驅動方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我要看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一個很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了某樣東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺出了錯或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數次意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 。 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看太多了 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技已經存在 , 可以協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子彼此交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到前面的三輛車 , 還有三輛車後面 , 到右邊 , 同時 , 鳥瞰視角 , 我們還能看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看那傢伙的前方有多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人要降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 不 , 車子不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路走下去 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會走在預先出版的路線上 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	很難做出合理的預測 , 預測車子在不久的將來會在哪裡 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使當你在車上時 , 有些摩托車人每小時85英里 , 我知道你有過這個經驗 , 不是 「 出去 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上大概在過去半個小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英里後 , 有人看過那傢伙 , 當一輛車看到那傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他的位置 , 速度 , 好估計 , 他會以每小時85英哩的速度繼續走85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他的車會在他的耳朵上低聲說: 「 順便說一下 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車 , 看一下 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達成目標 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的東西開始 , 就像分享車子間的位置資料 , 分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和攝影機在我的車子裡 , 我有一個很精確的概念 , 關於我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車在哪裡 , 以及他們要去哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道他們在哪裡 , 有點模糊 , 知道其他車在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車有同樣的數據 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 模擬了當模擬模擬結果 , 甚至在輕流量中 , 當車子共用gps資料時 , 我們把這項研究從電腦模擬中移到機器人的床上 , 進行真正的感測器 , 進行這些機器人的實際感測器:壓力攝影機、gps、二維雷射雷射雷射雷射 , 這些都是在後備系統中常見的 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也加上一段短距離通訊收音機 , 機器人會彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相抵觸時 , 它們能精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合更多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你收到太多的章節時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你得要優先考慮 , 那就是預測模型能協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你不會多注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點偏離軌道的人排除在前面 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會走下去 , 你知道怎麼做 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道哪些司機你需要警覺離開路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做些什麼 , 我們要如何警告每個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼可能會說: 「 你需要走出路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它取決於兩樣東西:一 , 車的能力 , 第二個駕駛能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人擁有很棒的車子 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 做些什麼 , 他們可能就不在緊急狀況的最佳位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一項分開的研究 , 做司機國家模式 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們能偵測到 , 如果駕駛向前看 , 向下看 , 看手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外事故 , 我們可以預測哪輛車 , 最好的位置是要走出路 , 去計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術是現今存在的 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常讓人沮喪的觀念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 談論其他車輛 , 說我們會在一片八卦的大道上走下去 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看看你的車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是件好事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望各位花點時間想想 , 如果你真的不希望身後的青少年知道你在煞車 , 你即將來到終點 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過自願分享我們的資料 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子看看你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金實現了他的夢想 , 透過一起飛進大氣層 , 體驗無重量的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	史蒂芬•霍金的彼得•戴曼迪斯在0g中在史蒂芬•霍金的史蒂芬•戴曼迪斯 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	那些認識我的人 , 知道我有多熱情 , 想要打開太空前線 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給全世界的重力專家──無重力的體驗 , 那真是太棒了 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我初次見到他是基因組學的archonx獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所持有的競爭 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一個團隊在十天內將100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的基因組一百個人 , 我們將它定序為其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特事件 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是要進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你到零的無重力中 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	唯一能體驗地球零度的方法 , 其實是用拋物飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿一架飛機 , 你飛過頂部 , 重量25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力--美國太空總署長度以來訓練他們的太空人 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始這樣做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始運作 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機構和一間公司飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你就會殺了這個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下來 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場新聞會議 , 我們宣佈我們要做一個零平面 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼他要上去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正處於不斷增加的風險 , 被災難摧毀......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果沒有進入太空 , 人類就不會有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在nasa車輛的後面 , 進入零角飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約二十個人捐款 , 我們捐款給十五萬美金給兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一個整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監測他的血液、心跳速率、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們有各式各樣的東西 , 例如緊急狀況 ; 神知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 太空梭起飛 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的另一半是羅恩•里希伯格 , 我小心地把他壓縮成零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力的真正體驗 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物蟲之後 , 你知道的 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他笑了 , 我們說: 「 走了 。 」
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二次拋物線鏡 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們實際上漂浮在牛頓爵士的霍格斯區因為霍金教授在劍橋舉辦了相同的椅子 , 艾薩克•牛頓 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四、第五、第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他很開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們一生中 , 我們正從這個星球上移下來 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這個史詩般的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫大衛•布林斯基在一個細胞內展現出令人震驚的動畫 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫了一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我來自一個稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在看真相和美麗的表達在科學中的藝術、真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都很美好 , 但他們都有很棒的東西 , 能為他們帶來真相和美 , 作為理想的科學和數學的理想 , 幾乎就像是科學家想約會的理想結合雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是令人敬畏的事物 , 意味著它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是很強大的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常在事實後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你可以把這些照片翻出來 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美 , 通常對不在科學領域的人來說是不可或缺的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來描述美麗的事物 , 通常只能理解語言和語法 , 研究真相和美的主題 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你觀察數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你觀察宇宙的常數 , 有一個人類理想 , 你可以看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字中進化 , 這些都是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導父親動畫的醫學插畫師以後 , 我嘗試做的是 , 他是雕塑家和我的視覺導師 , 我想要找出方法來幫助人們了解生物科學的真與美 , 透過動畫 , 用圖像 , 說故事 , 讓人們不見得有證據可以被教導 , 也能被教導 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生經常沉浸在一個環境中 , 她們學到的是有真相和美麗的主題 , 但她們被教導的方式卻被拿來比較 , 她們學到的事實和美 , 並不總是顯而易見 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是雞湯的老食譜 , 你煮雞肉 , 直到味覺消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生那樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我接到哈佛大學的robertlue打來的電話 , 在幾年前的分子和細胞生物學部門 。 他問我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛大學的醫學和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一項計畫 , 探索細胞 , 探索分子和細胞生物學的真與美 , 讓學生能了解更大的圖片 , 讓它們能夠記住這些事實 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有一塊由微機械所組成的大型巴士所構成的複雜城市 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械正處於生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是世界各地奈米技術人員的嫉妒 , 是自主導導導向、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 由胺基酸組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械的力量是細胞如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們會驅動細胞複製的方式 。 它們會影響我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅動我們的思想 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 想辦法把這個故事做成動畫 , 將是哈佛的生物維護中心 , 這個網站是哈佛大學為它的分子和細胞生物學系學生所設立的 , 除了所有的文學資料以外 , 所有的做法都被視覺組合在一起 , 這樣這些學生就可以從內部看出細胞的真相和美麗 , 並且能夠從中研究這個觀點 , 以此來研究它們的心靈感 , 使它們的生命能被發現 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子如何組合在一起 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你的巨噬細胞在微血管下流動 , 它們正在觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們正在從微血管壁上接收到來自細胞的信息 , 它們給的信息是 , 在外面的某處發炎 , 在那裡 , 它們看不見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓它們停止 , 讓它們內化 , 讓它們需要製造出各種各樣的零件 , 來改變它們的形狀 , 試著脫離這種微小的管道 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	這些分子馬達 , 我們得要和哈佛科學家及資料庫模型合作 , 模型原子是精確的分子 , 找出它們如何移動 , 找出它們的作用 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想辦法以一種真誠的方式來做這件事 , 讓發生了什麼事 , 但不太真實 , 細胞裡的緊密群會防止病毒發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘的讀者的消化版本 , 是我們製作的這部電影的第一個面向 。 這是一個持續進行的計畫 , 將要花四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看一下 , 看到細胞製造這些小步行機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為kinesin , 將這些巨大的負荷帶到相對大小的螞蟻身上 。
run the movie , please .	請跑這部電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器能驅動細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器都能彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們互相傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會導致細胞內發生不同的事 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造果蠅所需要的部件 , 由細胞核的分子所引發的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 如果沒有這些微機械的話 , 就不可能有生命了 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯的出席率真的很大 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做 「 kinesin 」 , 他拉著一把全新的製造蛋白質到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是到細胞膜 , 不論是用來製造或修復某樣東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人都有大約十萬個這種東西正在四處運作 , 目前 , 每一百兆個細胞中都有大約十萬個 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	不論你感覺多懶 , 你本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你回家時 , 我要你做的是想想這個 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想一些我們正在學習的關於細胞機械的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們了解了所有正在發生的事情 , 相信我 , 我們就知道一旦我們知道發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠掌握很多掌控我們的健康 , 掌握我們對未來的世代所做的事 , 以及我們將能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發現更多的真相 , 還有更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但令人驚訝的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 已經足以察覺細胞所需的作用 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 。 他們讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作 , 幫助我們身體的巨大實體 , 他們永遠看不到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃在她的車裡待了一年 , 看到了這個國家 , 但當憂鬱落入 , 她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅程變成無家可歸者 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她經歷成為美國無家可歸的無家可歸者 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會變遷、說故事、說故事、說故事、說故事、社會、社會、社會、說故事、故事、說故事、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:那一年 , 我無家可歸 , 無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是一位作家和記者 , 我也是一位瘋狂的好奇人 , 所以 , 22年來作為記者 , 我學會了很多新的東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作 , 在我父親同年二月去世之後 , 我決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡對我影響很大 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我這麼做時 , 我想要感受到和處理很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 。 我決定住在一台車裡待了一年 , 去做這件事就像一趟漫長的露營旅程 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把貓包起來 , 我的腐爛weiler和我的露營裝備裝在1975年的車裡 , 開車到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等於永久的結構 , 甚至是緊縮 , 以人的價值為衡量 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到 , 別人的負面感知會如何快速影響我們的現實 , 如果我們放下它的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車上是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 。 我經常吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但之後 , 我父親的死亡造成的憤怒和沮喪 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我得要有全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	當時很溫和的春天 , 變成了一個很熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在任何地方 , 都不可能停車 , 很顯然我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓跑過來 , 在車上打開窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗狗在照顧狗狗 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能時 , 我都會用辦公大樓的員工淋浴 , 卡車停止 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共房間洗衣服 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	在華氏80度以下的夜間溫度很少會降低 , 使得睡不著或無法睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰層在我的冰層融化了好幾個小時 , 感覺很悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起公寓 , 或負擔不起公寓 , 讓我有了腐爛的推力器和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄 , 所以我留在車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣使我無法走50英尺 , 到我車外的公共廁所時 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣候下降時 , 溫度降到冰凍之下 , 牠們留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停著不同的地點 , 這樣我才能避免被警察注意到和被警察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察注意
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺不到我人生的控制 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在車子裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走了 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒改變 , 我的智商還沒下學 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華 , 我的完整性 , 我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的東西都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但不知怎麼的 , 我改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入地探索了憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒有洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和任何人一樣 , 都很沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的 , 為什麼你會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒有把我視為無家可歸的人 , 但我做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的自殺傾向 , 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 沒人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯特 , 他是全國知名的記者 , 一直在談論我在國際電視台上談論我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是在提姆的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做這個講座的電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrusssert時 , 《見報》的前主持人在談論我的寫作 , 當我住在walmart停車場時 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為這已經到了我是作家 , 還是我是無家可歸的女性 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 找到提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀我的短論 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在貨車裡 , 和沙發衝浪之間的改變 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再被看不見了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 一同工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續把生活在車上或街上的犯罪化和罪犯化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 工作無家可歸 , 主要是看不見的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇過一個 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你把錢捐給下一個你遇見的乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 大家不是他們住的地方 , 他們睡在哪裡 , 或他們生活的情境隨時都在 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一輛沃爾瑪超市停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的《保險套》 , mechaiviravaida , 帶我們走過全國的大膽計劃 , 來提高它的生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克、有趣的 , 和非常有效的討論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、科學、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	契亞•維瓦里達:保險套如何讓泰國成為一個更好的地方 , 一個更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有許多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定採取行動 , 但我們並不是從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從家庭平台開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人能接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:到孩子們 , 去找媽媽 , 然後跟著家人計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	讓我帶各位回來 , 為何我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭中有7個孩子 , 成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女性說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們很少有醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把 「 不 」 視為 「 不 」 的問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去看護士和助產士 , 他們同時也是女性 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那是很棒的 , 但它只覆蓋了百分之二十的國家 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做些什麼 , 讓他們孤獨 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了普通人群 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色標誌下面我希望他們沒有這麼做 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很熟悉 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 而且他們很棒 , 他們自己練習了他們的家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地提供藥丸和保險套 , 在全國各個村莊 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們在那裡 。 我們去找被視為問題的成因者 , 來解決問題 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論有哪些人 , 你都能看到有女人的船 , 賣東西是漂浮的市場賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡找到的人 , 你會在泰國找到避孕品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不上宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教教會非常強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 聽著 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的那隻 , 不是黃色的黃色 , 拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶在吃藥和保險套上灑水 , 為家庭的聖經 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片被送到全國各地 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	有些村莊裡的僧人自己也做了同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與嘗試提供任何讓人類成為更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導家庭規劃 , 用新的字母a、出生、保險套、紫外線、血管切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們拿了一隻蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你扔了骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落在平常的規劃上 , 你就往前走 。
