like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如 「 媽媽每晚都會吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 繼續前進 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 , 很好 , 叔叔 , 繼續前進 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 再開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育和娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們有保險套的相關種族 , 我們有兒童的保險套冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久之後 , 保險套被稱為女生最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會把它做成這樣保險套就是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個微型貸款計畫 , 組織這個計畫的女性說: 「 我們只想借錢給做家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上借錢 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們所經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	經過35/36年之後 , 它仍然在發生 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 , 不是真正的銀行 , 而是基金微型貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來執行 , 由村民自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能幾乎看不到一個泰國人 , 總是女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著 , 我們以為我們會協助美國 , 因為美國一直在協助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要協助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定要為所有男人提供注射器 , 但特別是 , 美國人在排隊前面 , 直接送到大使館的居住地 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	旅館給我們一個非常適合的房間 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和功勞 。

we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫貧的唯一方法就是透過企業企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 那已經完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	這筆錢從公司到村莊 , 透過樹木移植 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種樹木 , 金錢進入他們的微型貸款基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。

and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你借錢之前 , 你需要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮的人 , 能夠取得信用的人一定是人權 。

here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	現在 , 終於在教育上 , 我們希望把學校改造成不受教育的地方 , 讓每個人成為終身學習中心 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能感覺像個朋友 , 但一個真正的朋友會給你一個微笑 。 在ted2013年 , 克萊納德•羅摩 , 一個智慧型手機驅動的機器人 , 可以和你一起走路 , 幻燈片你一張桌子的咖啡 , 和你做出可程式化的表情反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	克萊納多:一個迷你機器人 , 由你的手機驅動 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	舉手來說 , 在座有多少人家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	很多人都沒有 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好 , 其實是那些手 , 如果你不包含室巴 , 有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive嘗試解決的問題 , 我和其他20位在romotive的書呆子都很著迷於解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是8或80歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你得要建造一個小型可攜式機器人 , 它不僅是可以負擔得起的 , 而且它必須是人們想要回家 , 帶著孩子們回家的樣子 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不可能很詭異或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善的、可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個用你已經知道且愛你的iphone的機器人 , 來當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone的處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造一個可以用wi-fi和電腦視覺處理器的機器人 , 讓150美元的電腦視覺可行 , 這大約是過去機器人所付出的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他就在創造模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上是在用這個裝置上的攝影機來追蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我倒下 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他會轉向跟隨我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會嚇到和其他生物一樣 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像一隻有自己的寵物 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索這個世界 , romo已經累了如果我想要用romo來探索這個世界 , 我可以把他和其他ios設備連結起來 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	而romo會把視頻串到這個裝置 。
so i can see everything that romo sees , and i get a robot'seyeview of the world .	所以我可以看到romo所看到的一切 , 我得到了一個機器人的觀點 。
now this is a free app on the app store , so if any of you guys had this app on your phones , we could literally right now share control of the robot and play games together .	這是應用程式的免費應用程式 , 如果你們有人在手機上使用這個應用程式 , 我們現在可以一起控制機器人 , 一起玩遊戲 。
so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我很快地給你們看romo , 他在串流影片 , 所以你們可以看到我和ted的觀眾 。
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我來到romo前面 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我就可以開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	我可以帶他到處開車 , 拍下你們的照片 。
i've always wanted a picture of a 1 , 500person ted audience .	我一直都想要一張1 , 500個ted觀眾的照片 。
so i'll snap a picture .	我會拍一張照片 。
and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就像你在ipad上翻閱內容一樣 , 我可以在儀器上調整相機的角度 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	所以 , 你們所有人都透過romo的眼睛 。
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒表達自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以我可以進去 , 我可以說 , 讓我們來做romo興奮 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但romo最重要的是 , 我們想創造一個完全直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教別人如何開romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰想開一個機器人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你其實不需要和機器人在相同的地理位置來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上在任何兩個智能裝置之間串連了雙向音頻和影片 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以在瀏覽器上登入 , 有點像輪子上的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們先前談到遠端臨界 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	舉例來說 , 你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 她有iphone , 她媽媽買了她的機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放到機器人上 , 寄電子郵件給祖母 , 住在這個國家的另一邊 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那台機器人 , 和她的孫女玩隱匿號 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她可能只能看到她孫女每年一次或兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是現今romo可以做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的事物 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師 , 一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google開放式的架構上 , 叫做街區 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以拖著這些語義代碼 , 創造出任何你想要的機器人行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以模擬瀏覽器的行為 , 左邊是romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載它到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行它 , 在現實生活中執行程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有讓你驕傲的東西 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些無線網路的機器人 , 都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注在建造人人人都可以訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人學中 , 最具吸引力的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人轉變為人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你在家裡有機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道 , 要花10年或100億美金或大型人造機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將會取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 像是romo , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要給你所有機器人 , 我們等不及要看到你打造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和激進主義的伊莎貝爾會討論女性、創造力、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演講的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化、文化、文化、女人 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿爾德說過關於熱情的故事 ,
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 非常嚇人的是 , 在這裡 , 最聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴你們幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真理更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想傳達一個比我們共同人性更為真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我很感興趣 , 直到我最後寫了它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的神秘 , 所以我寫了關於巧合、預示、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去20年 , 我發表了幾本書 , 但我直到2006年二月 , 當我在義大利的冬季奧運會中帶著奧運 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在人們認得我在馬西的名人 , 我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你我四分鐘的名聲 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克典禮的組織者之一 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為國旗辯護者之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這絕對是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我可以從運動員的身分中得知 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以走在體育場 , 不用步行 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑物 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 三位奧運金牌獎得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 制服 , 要求我的測量標準 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有自己的遠景 , 在流行的動作中 , 看起來就像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我在土耳其 , 那裡充滿熱情的群眾在任何80個奧運隊伍都在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了所有比賽中的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但還有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一口雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風力的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 比訓練或運氣更重要的是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅海報覆蓋 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情在這裡 , 這不是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心就是驅使我們、決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中的角色所需要的:熱情心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要大把、異議者、冒險家、局外人和叛軍 , 他們會問問題、彎曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的人並不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只能做好之前的配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇到了其他旗幟:三位運動員 , 女演員蘇珊撒旦和蘇菲亞羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 兩個有熱情的女性:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 肯亞諾貝爾獎得主種了三千萬棵樹 。 藉由這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然 , 許多村莊的經濟條件 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	一位柬埔寨激進分子 , 他熱情對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 她的祖父賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 她們相信 , 和很年輕的處女做愛 , 會讓他們從愛滋病中治癒 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	每天有五、十五個客戶被迫要收到的妓院 , 如果她們反抗 , 她們就會受到電力的折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色的房間裡 , 我收到了我的制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的衣服 , 但距離我預期的米其林男士西服還很遠 。 真的不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像是冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但大部分的旗幟家 , 除了蘇菲雅洛倫 , 美麗和熱情的普遍象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅七十多歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很脆弱 , 很高 , 有很深的色彩 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你要如何有深色的坦承 ? 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪談問問: 「 她怎麼會看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答說: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直直直的 , 我沒有發出老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有一些免費的建議來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不發言、不咳嗽、不發臭、不跟自己說話 , 不至於遙控 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有那麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 聲響者宣佈奧運旗 , 順便一提 , 音樂起始於這邊的同一音樂 , aida遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅倫就在我面前 , 她比我高 , 不算毛毛毛髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 就像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 她肩上拿著旗子 。 我穿著我的尖端把旗子放在我的伸展手上 , 這樣我的頭其實就在旗子底下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有攝影機都是在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中我也出現了 , 儘管我常在蘇菲亞的腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都喜歡的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最好的四分鐘就是那些在奧林匹克體育場的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我先生在我說這句話時被冒犯了 , 雖然我向他解釋過 , 我們在私人身上做的事通常花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不該親自服用 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記它們 , 老時破壞我的大腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著我的心 , 帶著奧林匹克熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這是個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	1998年 , 這個地方是剛果的土桑難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上百分之八十的難民是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為剛果死亡營 , 因為那些沒有被殺的人會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕的女子 , 蘿絲•地圖 , 和她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看她的丈夫被虐待並殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她成功讓她七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生了雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪下麻痺的線 , 用她自己的頭髮綁起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她以營地指揮官的名字命名為雙胞胎 , 以取得他們的偏好 , 用黑色茶餵給他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當她的牢房裡的士兵強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著槍到她的頭上 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家人存活了16個月 , 接著 , 幸運的是 , 年輕的美國人 , 薩夏.查諾夫的熱情 , 他成功地把她放進美國救援機、羅塞.地圖和她的九個孩子 , 最後到達了亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 他們現在住在和茁壯的地方 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里 , 地圖意味著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書裡的主角是強壯且有熱情的女性 , 像是羅斯•繪圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不做這些 , 也不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都和女性合作過 。
i know them well .	我很了解他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代的時代 , 在世界末期 , 在父權天主教和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪在我五歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒到智利 , 所以沒人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 我的自由價格很高 , 且要質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能支付它 , 因為每次我收到的炸彈 , 我都能遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒保羅亞在二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續走下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有不可思議的鬥爭 。 女權主義約會了嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒和在場的優勢女性來說 , 但對世界上大部分的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被強迫要結婚、賣淫、強迫勞動 , 她們有不想要的孩子 , 或無法餵食 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們沒有控制身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被毆打 , 有時會因為不幸而被殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大部分的西方年輕女性被稱為女性主義者是侮辱者 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有很性感 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 女性主義從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我也遭受缺乏男性的苦難 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義不是死的 , 沒有意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 對女神的sake而言 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為蚜蟲 , 維納斯 , 或bimbo , 或任何你想要的東西 ; 名字並不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是一個孟加拉村莊的婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 她去診所當志工 , 在她的三週假期間 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好要清潔牙齒 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一個充滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一排婦女等了好幾個小時被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人處於極度痛苦的狀態 , 因為她有幾種腐爛的瘧疾 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道 , 唯一的解決方案就是拉出不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她的風險很大 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些諾伏卡因 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇氣和熱情 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她謀殺了禱告 , 繼續向前邁進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 鬆軟的病人親吻她 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生主義者把更多的牙齒拿出來 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正在等她丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像水母 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫脹到你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺美國 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但翻譯說明病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打敗她 , 因為她沒有家準備晚餐給他 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	儘管世界上三分之二的婦女在做勞動 , 他們擁有不到百分之一的世界資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於同一份工作 , 如果他們付錢 , 他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 而且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制她們自己的收入、繼承和財產的能力 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦權 , 她的孩子和家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家人繁榮 , 村莊繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去肯亞的一個村莊 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 解釋說土地是荒廢的 , 因為他們砍了樹 , 賣掉樹 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新的樹和水 , 掉下去 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	大約五、六年後 , 他們有森林 , 土壤被充足 , 村落被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最後退的社會 , 總是那些會讓女性失望的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善機構忽視 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給女性專案的每一塊錢 , 有20元給男性專案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們力量 , 會改變一切 , 不僅僅是科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起工作 , 連結、有知識、受教育 , 能帶給這個被偽造的星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是殘酷的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們所擁有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人都在問的一個根本的問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個保存生命的世界 , 生活品質對所有人都豐富的世界 , 不只是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月我看到費南多•博特歐在加州柏克萊圖書館的畫作 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊 , 卡里斯•波特歐的作品 , 還敢展示這幅畫 , 因為主題是阿布格拉伊監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 用的是大型的波特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的腦中或我的心中取得這些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的就是權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力的力量 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並強迫其他群體接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都在改變 , 但他們總是受惠 , 在這個例子中 , 技巧效應並不適用於經濟 , 完全適用 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從梯子的頂部到底部的虐待 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女性和孩子 , 特別是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最高的男性 , 她們也能虐待女人或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我得到了一些力量 , 透過性別、收入、種族、和階級 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時機是對我們的文明做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但為了真正的改變 , 我們需要全世界的女性能源 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要數不清的女性在權力的位置 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能源 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是年輕人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老年人無助 , 我們必須等待他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想有蘇菲雅羅倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 根據一個選擇 , 我寧願有勇氣的心 , 像是威加利馬塔伊 , 索瑪利媽 , 珍妮和羅斯地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的所有知識、能源、天賦和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們擺脫我們的炫耀 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦大小的城市中 , 有三千萬餐是用的 。 但是 , 所有的食物是從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡洛琳•史特爾討論了每天餵食城市的奇蹟 , 展示了古老食物路徑如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題、全球議題、
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史黛爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 , 如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們去一家商店或餐廳 , 或在一個小時內 , 就會有食物在等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 對於倫敦大小的城市來說 , 每天都要生產出足夠的食物 , 運輸、購買、煮飯、吃、丟掉這些東西 , 每天都要發生在地球上的每個城市 , 都很了不起 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的事物 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃 , 事實上我們和古老祖先一樣依賴自然界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著越來越多人搬進城市 , 越多的自然世界 , 被轉變成像我身後的那樣非凡的景觀 , 它是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 目的是要餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的地景 , 但很少人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的地景不僅僅是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著越多人搬進城市 , 我們就越多人吃肉 , 所以每年全球農作物中有三分之一的食物會被餵給動物 , 而不是我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於這需要三倍的穀物 , 實際上是十倍的穀物餵飽人類 , 如果是先通過動物的話 , 那不是非常有效率的方式來餵飽我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	問題也在惡化 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 據估計 , 我們所居住的城市數量會是兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 有兩倍的肉類和乳房消耗量 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和城市主義在手上升 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會帶來一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 挨餓的六十億人挨餓 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 事實上 , 如果我們繼續下去 , 這個問題就不太可能解決 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九百萬公頃的雨林被砍伐 , 來創造新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管同時 , 我們也失去了相當大量的耕種能力 , 來鹽和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要10卡路里才能生產西方的每一卡路里的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	即便如此 , 我們在生產大量成本的食物 , 我們也不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國生產的一半的食物現在被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這個長程結束時 , 我們甚至沒有適當地餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人肥胖 , 同時又有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球80%的食物貿易只由五間跨國企業所控制 , 這是一張可怕的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們去看未來 , 它是一種不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答稍微簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程是在古老的東邊 , 稱為 「 肥沃 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 正如你所見 , 正如你所見 , 正如你所看到的 , 正如你所看到的 ,
and it was also fertile .	同時也是肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 這兩種非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時也發生了 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並不意外 , 因為農業和城市是相互連結的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先第一次發現穀物 , 製造出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 來支撐永久的定居地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處的樣子 , 我們會看到它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產力的農場包圍 , 被大型的寺廟複雜所主導 , 像是烏爾 , 事實上 , 靈性化 , 中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為神殿安排收穫 , 聚集在穀物中 , 將它送給神 , 然後給予神神不吃人的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活都是由穀物所支配 , 以及維持它們的收穫所支配 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼回饋的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我所謂的 「 古老食物哩程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以進入海洋 , 讓它可以從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	在古代世界裡 , 只有這樣做 , 因為要在路上運輸食物是非常困難的 , 差不多就是這樣 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快就消失了
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬很有效率地在像凱斯和埃及這樣的地方打仗 , 只為了取得他們的穀物保留地 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張真的是一長串的 , 畫出軍事化的購物圈 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡事實 , 我只需要提一下:羅馬以前是從倫敦進口牡蠣的 , 在某個階段 , 我覺得這很不凡 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	羅馬透過它的胃口 , 塑造了它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 在工業界也發生了另一件事 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它來自thames , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	路從他們走到廉價的路上 , 那是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看這些街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是從河流進來的 。 同樣的東西 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比爾辛辛格很有名的是倫敦的魚市場直到1980年代中期才開始運作
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	真的 , 仔細想想 , 這真的很不尋常 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都在用行動電話遊蕩 , 看起來像磚頭 , 有點像是在港口捕魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市中的食物:一旦它根入城市 , 它們很少會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是很不一樣的 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物會走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉都來自西北 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦著名的肉市場 , 位在那邊 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽從東加利亞到東北
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像氣象女性這樣做 。 總之 , 鳥類會用腳保護著牠們的腳 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當他們進入便宜的東端時 , 他們就被賣掉了 , 這就是為什麼被稱為 「 家禽 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看工業時代的任何城市地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物進來 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物的形狀 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名字 , 給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在過去的人生中 , 是你在星期五去買你的魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的影像 , 你可以看到 , 住在這樣的城市中 , 很難知道你的食物從哪裡來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 假如你有星期日午餐 , 可能是你的窗外流血或流血的機率大約三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的圖片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的火車乘客是豬和綿羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們因為視力和心智而被屠殺 , 在鄉下某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們以鐵路進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首先 , 它可以成為第一次 , 種植城市 , 大小和形狀 , 在任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去的城市被地理限制 ; 他們以前必須透過非常困難的實體方式來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們被地理限制了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所看到的 , 從倫敦的地圖上看到的 , 在火車出現的九十年後 , 它從一個很容易被動物送進來的小小圓點 , 以此類推 , 到一個很大的海綿 , 要不管是腳上、動物或人類 , 都很難餵飽 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是開端 。 火車來了之後 , 真的是這個過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市的最後解放 , 完全和大自然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是那種沒有氣味的城市 , 沒有混亂的城市 , 絕對沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們把食物送到車上 , 開車到郊區的某個地方 , 帶著一週的購物回來 , 想知道到底該怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們與食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物 , 以前是市中心 , 在邊緣的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社交活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前煮飯 ; 現在我們加入水或一點蛋 , 如果你做蛋糕或其他東西的話 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是在包裝上讀到標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不重視食物 , 我們不相信食物 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再相信它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	我們不再重視它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統最諷刺的一點是 , 他們做出了他們承諾要讓生活更加困難的東西 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市可以在任何地方建立城市 , 實際上它們能讓我們與我們最重要的關係脫離 , 那就是我們和大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 它們也讓我們依賴它們能傳遞的系統 , 如同我們所見 , 它們是無法永續發展的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那麼 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯•摩爾在問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他書《烏托邦》的頭條 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列半獨立的城邦 , 如果聽起來很熟悉 , 一天之間的走路 , 每個人基本上都是農人 , 在他們的後花園中種植蔬菜 , 一起吃飯 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為你可以說 , 食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即使從來沒有這樣做 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個非常有名的烏托邦願景 , 伊伯內斯霍華的《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列半獨立的城邦 , 一小片大都市的東西 , 帶著耕地 , 連接到鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被認為是他願景的訂購原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但跟霍華德的這個願景沒有關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦想法的問題是 , 他們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它的產量是希臘的兩倍 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好的地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 , 一個有想像力的東西 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類的深層問題 , 讓它不太能被使用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 來自古希臘文 「 西托 」 、 「 為食物 」 、 「 湯波 」 的替代方案 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以把食物當作一個非常強大的工具 , 一個概念性工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	如果我們這樣做 , 西托邦看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我想這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是狗臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是食物在生活的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們花時間陪伴它 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這就是我們社會中糧食應當的地方 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非你有這樣的人 , 你不能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便一提 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 會想 , 誰會計劃 , 會盯著一堆原生蔬菜 , 並且認得它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這種人 , 我們就不能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選擇這個 , 因為這是一個人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路、市場 , 在那裡 , 食物在當地生長 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有了這一點 , 你就不能有這種地方種植的食物 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 而不只是一個零和的商品 , 在一些看不見的地獄裡 。
cows with a view .	牛有著視野 。
steaming piles of humus .	大堆的 「 嗡 」 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上就是把整件事結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區專案 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	它是一個溫室 , 孩子們會告訴所有關於食物和種植他們自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一棵叫kevin的植物 , 或者它屬於一個叫kevin的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但不管怎樣 , 這些企劃試圖與大自然重新連結的計畫是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 西托邦 , 對我來說 , 真的是一種看待方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 西托邦已經存在於小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是要把它們加在一起 , 用食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就不再把城市看成大型、大都市化、無生產力的怪物 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們將看到它們更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免的 , 具有共生關係的 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是很棒的形象 , 因為我們不需要再製造像這樣的食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要考慮永續發展 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖片總結出我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這是一種重新概念化的食物如何塑造我們的生活 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是從650年前開始 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是阿布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂的 「 好政府的寓言 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	現在 , 我想問我們 , 阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂 , 如果他今天畫出這張影像 , 會是什麼樣子 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好政府的寓言會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	我們得要問 , 我們得要開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們就是吃什麼的 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解 , 世界也是我們吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為一個非常強大的工具 , 來塑造世界變得更好 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	卡倫•阿姆斯壯在21世紀的宗教角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 還是我們共通的 ? 她檢視世界信仰的催化劑 , 來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、2009年tedglobal、暴力、暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重現黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我感到很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我敏銳地意識到同情心在世界各大宗教的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都進化了他們自己的黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它出現在一個正面的版本中 , 「 總是把他人當作你想要被治療的所有人 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面版本: 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現它給予你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 將痛苦在其他人身上發揮 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很棒 , 也因為它很有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施黃金法則時 , 如同混亂所說: 「 整天 , 」 不只在做好事時 , 還要回到貪婪和自負的生活 , 每天都要做 , 你從世界的中心來拒絕自己 , 放在那裡 , 超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你到一個名為 「 上帝 」 的存在 , nirvana , rama , tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的自我存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道很多時間 , 這對宗教生活是很重要的 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有了一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人聚在一起 , 宗教領袖聚在一起時 , 他們會爭論廢除教條 , 或說出仇恨的議會 , 或反對同性戀或類似的事情 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到當我和一群宗教人談話時 , 有點像是在表達他們的臉 , 因為人們常常想做對的事 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼這麼感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書籍研究帶我進入二十一世紀 , 讓我能和比我想像中更廣泛的觀眾交談 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到很迫切 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們沒有辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 所以我們對待所有人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 不論他們是誰 , 彷彿他們和我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來傳給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代最偉大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 卻被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種有想像力的同理心的行為 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有選擇 , 對我來說似乎是如此 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續提出或強調我們信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 或者我們可以回到拉比希爾 , 一位年長的耶穌現代人 , 當他站在一條猶太教義上時 , 他說: 「 這對你的鄰居來說是有害的 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那是托拉和其他一切都只是評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	拉比和早期教會的父親說 , 教堂的任何詮釋都說 , 教條的任何詮釋都不合法 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要復興那個精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不僅會發生 , 因為愛情的精神會降低我們 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須實現這一點 , 而且我們能用ted所介紹的現代溝通來做到 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有夥伴的反應感到極大的鼓舞 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人 , 會使用最近在新加坡社會中所使用的治癒分裂 , 國會的一些成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一場藝術展 , 主導藝術家會帶領人們、年輕人 , 並展現出慈悲心也源於所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在歐洲 , 穆斯林社區在舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰中同情心的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那裡 , 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 我們錯過了 , 專注於相信abstrusse的教條 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定永遠會引起行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在我死去的那一天工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續讓我們的夥伴們去做兩件事 , 去教育和刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們已經失去同情心了 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這只是對某人感到抱歉的意思 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但當然 , 如果你只是想一想 , 你不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 要協助分解一些我們對他人的刻板印象 , 把我們從彼此分開來 。
the same applies to educators .	教育家也一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到動態、動態和挑戰同情生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它需要急性智能 , 而不僅僅是舒服的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想呼籲學者去探索他們自己和其他人傳統中的同情心 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵不友善的言論的敏感度 , 如此一來 , 因為人們有這章節 , 不論他們的信念或缺乏信念 , 他們覺得有能力挑戰不友善的言論 , 不友善的宗教領袖 , 他們的政治領袖 , 來自工業界的領袖 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過把這篇文章放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在舊世界裡 , 一大群人坐在一間房間裡 , 還在說另一句話 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹一個全新的思考方式和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted的美妙之處 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專長 , 如果我們加入這一切 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有時候問題似乎很有吸引力 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但最後我想引用一句英國作家的話 , 他是牛津作家 , 我不常引用c.s.lewis 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 從我讀書的時候 , 一直困在我腦海裡 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四個愛》裡 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他分辨出愛情之間的差別 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友誼做比較 , 當兩個人站在旁邊 , 如同肩膀肩膀肩膀 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們能成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我很強烈地感受到 , 在我們在vey的小型決心時 , 所有不同的說服的人聚在一起 , 一起合作 , 一起合作合作 , 為了一個共同的目標 , 把差異融化 。
and we learn amity .	我們學到的是同性戀 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 了解彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。

she parks her dirigible , lowers the anchor rope and climbs down for a closer look inside .	她停了她的數量 , 降低了繩子 , 爬下去 , 再更仔細地觀察她的內部 。
the text here is right side and upside down so that you are forced to turn the book around , and you can see it from ground point of view and from her point of view looking in the hole , getting a different kind of perspective , moving you around the space . particularly appropriate in a building that can contain perfectly a sphere dimensions of the diameter being the same as the distance from the center of the floor to the center of the oculus .	這裡的文字是對的 , 向下的 , 這樣你就被迫轉過來 , 從地面的角度看 , 從她的角度看 , 帶著不同的觀點 , 移動你 , 特別適合在一個建築中 , 容納著直徑的一維空間 , 和在八月中心的距離一樣 。
unfortunately for her , the anchor line gets tangled around the feet of some boy scouts who are visiting the pantheon , and they are immediately yanked out and given an extraordinary but terrifying tour of some of the domes of rome , which would , from their point of view , naturally be hanging upside down .	不幸的是 , 對她來說 , 這條線環繞著一些拜訪萬神廟的男孩偵查員 , 他們馬上就被拉出來了 , 給了一些奇特但可怕的旅程 , 一些羅馬的圓頂 , 從他們的角度來看 , 自然會被往下掉 。
they bail out as soon as they get to the top of saint ivo , that little spiral structure you see there .	一旦他們抵達聖象群的頂端 , 就會保釋你所看到的小螺旋結構 。
she continues on her way over piazza navona .	她繼續走下去 , 穿越了帕札納維納 。
notices a lot of activity at the tre scalini restaurant , is reminded that it is lunchtime and she's hungry .	注意到在trescoalini餐廳裡的許多活動 , 都提醒了它是午餐時間 , 她餓了 。
they keep on motoring towards the campo de' fiori , which they soon reach . ajax the dog is put in a basket and lowered with a list of food into the marketplace , which flourishes there until about one in the afternoon , and then is completely removed and doesn't appear again until six or seven the following morning .	牠們繼續向柬埔寨的菲利里移動 , 很快地牠們就抵達 。 雅克斯把狗放進籃子裡 , 裝滿一份食物到市場上 , 直到下午 , 牠才會浮起來 , 然後完全移除 , 直到六、七個早上才開始 。
anyway , the pooch gets back to the dirigible with the stuff .	總之 , 糞便會回到可怕的東西上 。
unfortunately , when she goes to unwrap the prosciutto , ajax makes a lunge for it .	不幸的是 , 當她去揭開校園時 , ajax會為此吃午餐 。
she's managed to save the prosciutto , but in the process she loses the tablecloth , which you can see flying away in the upper lefthand corner .	她成功地拯救了這個學徒 , 但在這個過程中 , 她失去了桌布 , 你可以在左上角看到飛走 。
they continue without their tablecloth , looking for a place to land this thing so that they can actually have lunch .	他們不用桌布繼續下去 , 找一個地方降落這個東西 , 這樣他們才能真的吃午餐 。
they eventually discover a huge wall that's filled with small holes , ideal for docking a dirigible because you've got a place to tie up .	他們終於發現了一座充滿了小洞的巨大牆 , 理想的把一個可怕的地方綁起來 , 因為你還有一個可以綁起來的地方 。
turns out to be the exterior wall that part of it that remains of the coliseum , so they park themselves there and have a terrific lunch and have a spectacular view .	原來是哥倫斯留下來的外圍牆 , 所以他們會在那裡停下來 , 吃很棒的午餐 , 看上去很棒 。
at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	午餐結束時 , 他們將chor解開 , 他們從卡拉浴場 , 穿過城市的牆壁 , 接著 , 一個廢棄的大門 , 決定再看一眼西斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 上面有一道閃電 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 那是個問題:他們太靠近了 , 當你在可怕的情況下 , 你必須非常小心地注意刺激 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	所以這有點像是把她的故事帶到一個結論中 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , marcello有點懶惰 , 但他一直在工作 , 直到無時無刻都在工作 。
so , the alarm goes off and it's five to 12 or so .	所以 , 警報消失了 , 大約是五到十二歲 。
he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 跳到他的摩托車上 , 種族穿越整個城市 , 超越聖馬利亞德拉的教堂 , 沿著巷子 , 穿過遊客的街道 , 每輪都要走過安靜的羅馬背景 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	他移動的速度 , 我希望我建議這張小小的圖片 , 可以轉過頭看 , 因為底部和文字上面有文字 , 其中一張是顛倒的圖片 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續前進 , 接近一個不懷疑的服務生 , 他試圖在一個脆弱的白葡萄酒杯醬給坐在餐廳外面的餐廳外面的餐桌上 。
waiter catches on , but it's too late .	服務生接住了 , 但已經太遲了 。
and marcello keeps moving in his scooter .	馬歇羅繼續前進 。
everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	從這個時候起 , 他所看到的一切都有點受到語言影響 , 但繼續前進 , 因為這個傢伙有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	除去一些支架 。 羅馬仍然是不平凡的地方 , 原因之一 , 是因為支架和決心要維持結構 , 一個城市持續成長和適應它所發現的特定時間的需求 , 或我們發現它自己 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	穿過pazzaderotonda , 又在萬神廟前 , 又醒來 , 終於開始工作了 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	馬賽利歐 , 事實證明 , 是64輛公車的驅動力 , 如果你在64輛公車上 , 你知道它的驅動力和馬塞洛在他的台上展示的一樣 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	最後是卡萊托 。 你看到他在左上角的公寓 。
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他正在看著他的桌子 , 他打算在晚上向他的女友提出這個建議 , 他希望它能完美 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他把蠟燭拿出來 , 中間有一朵花 , 試圖找出要把盤子和眼鏡放哪裡 。
but he's not happy ; something's wrong .	但他並不開心 , 有些事是錯的 。
the phone rings anyway , he's called to the palazzo .	總之 , 電話響了 , 他被叫去palazo 。
he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他在一段很好的短片上逃跑 , 但和我們剛才看到的旅程相比 , 他在逃跑 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道carletto , 因為他在娛樂上 , 他在電視上 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他其實是在電視修復 , 這就是為什麼人們知道他 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的數字 。
he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他到達了帕拉索 , 到達前門前的大門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入庭院 , 和客戶談話 , 他告訴他 , 在帕拉索有一場災難 ; 沒有人在工作 , 足球比賽上來 , 群眾變得有點不安 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後漸漸地把他的路往上延伸到建築的頂端 , 公寓 , 檢查每個電視 , 檢查每一個連結 , 希望找出問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他終於成功了 , 大樓梯接著一個小樓梯 , 直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開了閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 有一張桌布包著建築物的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題解決了 , 帕拉索的每個人都快樂 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要用一個完美的桌子 , 等著她抵達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是我第一次嘗試 , 但似乎還不夠實質 , 可以傳達我想要傳達羅馬的內容 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 好吧 , 我就來做吧 , 我會進去 , 下面我會展示這些東西在成長 , 展示它們為什麼會塑造它們的樣子等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我就想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最喜歡的部分和碎片放進萬神廟裡 , 把尺寸放進去 , 這樣你就可以看見聖誕節的頂端 , 西斯提烏斯的金字塔和巴曼特拉曼特的聖殿旁邊 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一張圖 , 所以我想也許是皮蘭西要去見escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你看我已經開始失去控制權了 , 也失去了希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常薄的藍線 , 會穿過這個東西 , 有點像是把一切連結在一起的軌跡 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不只是收集和儲存資訊的好方法 , 它是一系列的 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層剝下來 ; 我們認為他們是頁面 , 用某種方式來做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成是層級的 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是一個層級的地平層 , 垂直層層 , 我心想 , 只要把頁面撕下來 , 就能讓我用正確的方式來思考 , 讓我可以向你們展示層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部份建築的牆壁都包含了傷疤 ; 這些結構的傷疤數世紀以來 , 而不是被撕裂 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一張摺疊頁 , 讓你把它展開 , 你可以看到我所謂的疤組織背後的意思 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製造小型的窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人要來或其他東西 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應都被埋在黏土底下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這個palazzo的頁面向你們展示裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也能讓你們看看在其中一個偉大的建築角落 , 裡面有大型石塊 , 或是磚塊和黏土所做的假石塊 , 通常更常是如此 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你帶到一條狹窄的小街上 , 用雙重摺疊頁面 , 如果你跟我一樣 , 小時候讀一本pop-up的書 , 你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你的頭包裹起來 , 在那短暫的時間內 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我並沒有做任何更複雜的事 , 比起摺疊頁面 ,
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我想 , 或許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神廟 , 前面的pazzallotonda 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開這本書 , 只要我打開它90度 , 我們就在萬神廟的前面 , 我們在看上方 , 往下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把這本書的另一面翻過來 , 我們就在萬神殿前看過廣場 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊品 , 沒有把戲 , 只是一本沒有打開整個過程的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我心想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺紙和唯一開放的書結合在一起 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們走進了萬神廟 , 它不斷地成長 , 等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我站在正確的軌道上 , 但它失去了人類的品質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想要讓人們注意書 , 一路上收集資訊 , 總是一件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 震撼了我 , 成為一個 「 抓住我 」 的標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是蜂巢鴿 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那段旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題有效 , 使用它 , 那會是一段旅程 , 穿過羅馬 , 展示出我喜歡羅馬的東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	這是一隻鴿子 , 坐在教堂的頂端 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天離開 , 做正常的鴿子 。 回來 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網包覆著 , 這鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	它現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另外一個地方 , 這讓我可以經歷我最喜歡的東西的目錄 , 我們從高度的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它得要回去和家人一起生活 , 那不一定是件好事 , 但它確實會讓鴿子再次聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一生都在照顧生病鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方 , 讓他們去危險的地方 , 什麼不 , 他們會和這個傢伙交朋友 , 學習為他做招術 , 在午餐時間和其他類似的事情上娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	這種老人和鴿子之間的關係是真實的 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束後就生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 艾爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三、四天後出現 , 看不見他 , 他住在這個小小的車庫裡 , 拼他的名字和飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到了足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 拉紅氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘記提到這一點:每當他失去了鴿子時 , 他就會把鴿子放到城市的牆上 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在老羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有埋藏在牆壁裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我以為這是一個非常動人的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	真的很長一段時間了 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了...再一次 , 如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事不會去任何地方 , 我只想出標題 , 希望書名會把我趕出正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時候它會把我專注在我身上 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁面 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題 , 最終帶我到我定居的解決方案 , 這個故事是關於一個年輕女子的故事 , 她在羅馬城牆外送訊息給城市中的羅馬人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子飛上亞洲 。

this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大部份的居住鴿子都不做的事:它需要那條景色路線 , 我覺得這台裝置是必要的 , 把這本書延伸到四頁以外 。

this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為這是一個完整的基準化 , 否認任何規則的觀點 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點法則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出在這裡消失的點 , 幾對在火星上 , 還有幾位在克雷蒙亞的其他地方 。
