i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的零件:聖母瑪麗亞•德拉斯 , 有一個足球 , 有一點鳥翅膀沒有發生 , 所以我得要重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看到聖母瑪麗亞德拉的速度 , 這些書真的很靈活 , 令人難以置信的互動 , 轉過頭來看 , 另一方面 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到紅線所捕捉到的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥類把自己拉到中世紀的高塔上 , 剩下的少數中世紀大樓 , 朝聖誕老人的教堂 , 向下看 , 向下看 , 向下看 , 我們已經提到 , 看過了幾次 , 看到了 , 流過了四條河流的伯尼斯塔 , 然後超越了偉大的布魯米羅米諾•桑迪諾 , 停止了26英尺長的距離 , 停止了我們的呼吸道 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們可以四處流動 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不需要擔心重力在這個特定時刻 , 所以這幅圖可以以任何方式在頁面上被引導 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會有點興奮 ; 這並不讓人意外 , 用這種方式模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	穿過我剛剛提到的美好的牆壁 , 美麗的雕刻在尼龍 「 崛起 」 上方的牆上 , 等等 。

straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一個小窗戶 , 進入閣樓 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿部移除訊息 , 這是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板時 , 我們看到他正在做的事 , 事實上 , 鴿子剛剛拍攝的旅程地圖 , 紅線延伸了所有的視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 所以我們完成了這個關於理解的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究者skylarstibbit在自我組裝上 , 而不是建造東西 , 我們可以創造一些材料 , 更像dnazips本身 , 這是個很大的概念 。 tibbits告訴我們三項關於自我組裝未來的計畫 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天空的tibbits:我們能製造製造製造製造自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向你們展示我們創造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築和機器就會自我組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	我將向你們展示我所相信的 , 是目前製造業的狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造狀態中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、令人興奮的新技術 , 鋼鐵、水泥、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年--[組裝時間]250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以摺疊一萬奈秒 , 或用三十億鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統中有這麼多複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都還要有效率 , 遠遠比我們能建造的任何東西都還要複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有一點很有趣 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將它轉化到我們的建築環境中 , 那就有一些令人興奮的潛力 , 可以用來建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的實體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的複雜性 , 來建造建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要把它解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的零件 , 可以把這些序列拿來摺疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 讓它能夠啟動 , 讓我們的零件能夠從程式中摺疊 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤控權來確保我們成功地建立了我們想要的東西 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些計畫 , 我的同事和我在麻省理工正在努力達成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩個是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模的可重組機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們嵌入了機械裝置 , 感測器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼你想要摺疊的是什麼 , 變成一連串的角度-120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 120 , 負120 , 類似這樣的東西 ; 一連串的角度 , 或轉 , 然後你將序列透過弦傳遞 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都會收到它的訊息 , 負120個它會轉到那邊 , 檢查是否到那邊 , 然後把它傳給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師在這個計畫上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的能帶來光明:它真的很可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 成千上萬美元 , 製造了這個八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個放大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人放到每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看被動性大自然 , 或被動地試圖進行調整編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它進一步進一步 , 它試圖進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上是計算最基本的基礎積木 , 數位邏輯大門 , 直接嵌入你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是nandgate 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 它是通往你的電腦的大門 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 當你在建造你的磚塊時 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前面的磚塊中放出來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	再給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	意思是 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它會計算它以前所做的事 , 你說它要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間上下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1、1]輸入等於0的輸出 , 就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是1個輸出值 , 就會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們所有的資訊都嵌入其中 , 說明了什麼是被建構出來的 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱它為自動複製 , 因為你的結構包含了精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有的當地資訊都嵌入在上面 , 告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可能有爬上去讀取的東西 , 可以輸出一個到一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 , 沒有外部指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個專案叫做 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是我們目前最令人興奮的例子 , 被動自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要可重組性和可編程性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要左轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每個單位是否該轉左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖動鏈 , 它會摺疊成任何你編程的組合 , 例如 , 螺旋 , 或這個例子 , 兩個立方體相互相相對 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以程式任何三維的形狀或維度的二維空間 , 完全被動地進入這個鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們有新的可能性可以自我組裝、複製、修復我們的實體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可編寫能力 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從中 , 你有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是很驚人的平行和分散式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	對此 , 它是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以 , 我認為我在這裡所展示的這些計畫只是一個小步 , 邁向這個未來 , 如果我們實行這些新科技 , 來創造一個新的自我組合世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了非洲大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底最深的一點 。 下一代要探究什麼 ? 生物學家和探險者nathanwolfe提出了這個答案:幾乎每一件事 。 他說 , 帶著這個不可思議的世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學、科學、生物學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾夫:要去探索什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一個偉大的二十世紀探險家羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的時代 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列的探險 , 來到未知的地區 , 例如在戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來他說 , 印第安納瓊斯人物的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特時 , 我給一群中學學生公開講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡要告訴各位 , 如果在ted演講中 , 比在座的演講更親密的話 , 它會試圖注意到一群45分鐘課程中的一千二歲人 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	演講結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 我就一直困住了 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為有很多人有一種感覺 , 地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 在下一代 , 他們得要去外太空或深海 , 才能找到重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這是真的嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有任何東西可以讓我們探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想起生物歷史中我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一個看不見的世界的探險家 , 馬丁烏斯•貝吉尼克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草病的成因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是把被感染的果汁從菸草植物中取出 , 將它過濾成更小、更小的過濾器 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到了那個時候 , 他覺得一定有某種比當時所知最小型的生命形式還要小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的謎團找了一個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱它為 「 毒藥 」 的拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們開啟了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒組成地球上大部分的基因信息 , 遠超過所有其他生命形式的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 已經有很大的實際應用 , 和這個世界有關 , 比如根除天花 , 疫苗的出現是對子宮頸癌的先鋒 , 我們現在知道 , 大部分是由人類的帕羅馬病毒造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道生命形式是如何組成地球上大部分基因信息的 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了不可思議的工具 , 來探索那些看不見的世界 , 例如深度定序 , 讓我們能做得遠遠超過表面 , 從特定物種看個人基因組 , 再來看看整個新陳代數 , 微生物群落在我們身邊 , 記錄這些物種的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧用在土壤、皮膚、所有東西之間 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在常常這樣做 , 來辨識出爆發的原因 , 完全是造成它們的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上都拿了一個鼻子 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常用這種方法來尋找呼吸道病毒 , 比如流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到一些常見的猜測 , 當然 , 很多人類的基因信息 , 同時 , 細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分來自你鼻子內完全沒有傷害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常非常令人驚訝的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息並不符合任何我們從未見過的植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些研究這類資料的小團體 , 我們當中少數人已經開始稱之為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的任何東西 , 而是相當於在我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡百分之二十的基因信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達百分之四十到五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對不穩定的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 也不能被輸入或配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們以為這是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著他們越來越準確 , 我們決定了這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 或者至少其中一些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設只存在於它們的暗物質中 , 存在著非常非常令人興奮的可能性:在這個生命中埋藏在這個基因信息中 , 代表著尚未被辨識的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c、g , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命階級 , 例如beijerinck , 將徹底改變我們對生物學的本質 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	或許可以讓我們辨識出癌症的成因 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的爆發病源 , 或是在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 和史丹佛大學的同事、加州理工學院和加州理工學院的同事們一起 , 我們目前正在開始一項計畫 , 來探索生物暗物質 , 來探索新的生命存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 生命形式是地球上大部分的基因信息組成的 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆 , 我們可能完全不知道一種新的生活階級 , 真的就在我們的鼻子底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	沒錯 , 我們可能對地球上所有的大陸作了圖表 , 我們可能已經發現了所有外面的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的善良為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的一課 , 像是威斯康辛州的貝洛特年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為如果我們這樣說 , 就會是這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為的全部故事是全部的 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在你選擇探索的領域中 , 去探索暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊有未知的事物 , 他們只是等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch把理論物理放在後埋葬上 , 來討論更迫切的問題:人類的生存 。 他說 , 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 就是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、全球議題、物理、科學、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在宇宙中的我們位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這樣做 , 但我想要從大家已經知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	事實上 , 首先 , 是歷史上大部分人都知道的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其它的地球 , 都是獨一無二的適合來維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像過去的思想和我們現在的存在一樣 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	想法是 , 在太空船外面 , 宇宙是不可思議的 , 而內部是我們所擁有的 , 我們所仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都知道的 , 與大部分人類歷史所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如同史蒂芬•霍金所說 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面上的化學雕像 , 繞著一個典型的恆星繞著一個典型的星球 , 位在一個典型的銀河系的郊區 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家所知道的這兩件事的第一件事就是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二件事是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是如果你把這兩種真相視為深刻的真相 , 來告知你人生的決定 , 那麼他們似乎有點衝突彼此 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	他們是的 。 讓我先從第二個例子開始 , 很典型嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們來看看四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 然後我們看到一面牆 , 化學氣囊 , 這完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你要做的只是朝同一個方向走幾百英里 , 回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆或化學污垢 , 你看到的就是藍色的行星 。 如果你更進一步 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系 , 和恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不典型的宇宙 , 因為星星會進入銀河系 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中大部分的地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們再往外走 , 直到我們在銀河系外面 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 銀河系有著巨大的銀河系 , 螺旋臂在我們面前擺動 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們仍處於一個典型的宇宙中 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 你要到達一千倍的距離 , 到達一個星系間的空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	在宇宙中典型的地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的代價下 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 從星系間空間的角度呈現出銀河空間 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 請看 , 這樣我們就可以看得到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美你可以看到 , 在星系間的空間中是完全漆黑的 , 漆黑的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	如果你看著最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星就會爆炸成超新星 , 你就直接盯著它看 , 當它照亮你時 , 你甚至無法看到一個滑翔生物 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙的大小和暗度 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星很亮 , 很聰明 , 但它會讓你死於數年的光年 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間 , 到目前為止 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡的溫度也很低 , 絕對零度超過三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	這是非常空的 。 真空狀態下的密度比目前地球上最好的科技能創造的高達一百萬倍 。 這就是典型的地點 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈關回來嗎 ? 謝謝
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們如何知道一個遙遠的環境 , 如此不同 , 外星人 , 和我們以前習慣的任何環境 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球 , 我們的環境 , 以我們的方式 , 正在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這意味著什麼 ? 嗯 , 看看比我們剛剛從這裡看到的還要遠一點 , 用望遠鏡 , 你會看到看起來像恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 夸薩 」 。 夸薩爾原本是指量子星體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像恆星 , 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年後 , 星系中心的物質崩塌成一個超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了重力崩塌的部分能量 。 其中一些物質以巨大的噴射流形式 , 以光明的角度照亮了葉子 , 我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不可能和這台噴射機的物理更不一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法即時存活下來 。 語言瓦解 , 試圖描述其中一個噴射機中會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像是體驗到超新星爆炸 , 但在尖端的範圍 , 一次又幾百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這台噴射機在數十億年後發生在宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學污垢可以準確地描述、模型、預測 , 並解釋 , 最重要的是 , 你在現實中所發生的事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 一個大腦 , 包含了一個精確的運作模式 , 其它夸薩爾 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的超平面形象 , 雖然它包含了它 , 還包含了解釋性的模型 , 體現出相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這才是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 其中一個結構和另一個結構相似 , 就是隨著時間的增長 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那個實體物體 , 和它們可能不同 , 仍然可以體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間不斷地實現 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是種不同的化學氣味 。 這種化學氣味有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構 , 包含著不斷增加的精確度 , 萬物的結構 。 這個位置 , 而非宇宙中的其他位置 , 是它本身的結構和因果的本質 , 包含了整個實體現實的本質 。 到目前為止 , 不論是無知 , 物理定律允許這個定律 , 甚至允許它發生 , 是物理世界最重要的事項之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	太陽系和我們的環境 , 如何在我們與宇宙其餘的關係中取得這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬霍金的提議有一個事實 , 我是說 , 這是真的 , 但這是錯誤的強調 。 一件事是 , 它沒有用任何特殊的物理 。 沒有特殊的干擾 , 沒有奇蹟涉入 。 它只用了我們這裡的三樣東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 , 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 沒有知道製造電腦的方法 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要精力來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體能夠影響我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放式的知識、解釋來說 , 都是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	比方說 , 牛頓重力定律大約在三百年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但 , 我們過去做過的證據 , 已經在地球上數十億年前 , 地球上每一平方公尺上下降 , 之後會持續落下數十億年 。 其他科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學最基本的真理 , 只是為了地球上取得的證據 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的所在地 , 有證據 , 也有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三種為開放式知識創造而設立的設備 , 是他們最低的可能供給 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它是空的 , 它是冷的 , 它是暗的 。 還是嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像一下 , 在星系間的空間裡有一個立方體 , 跟我們家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 立方體是非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸的土地足以製造一個自給自足的太空站 , 上面有一群科學家 , 致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 除了現代科技之外 , 還能從星系間空間收集氫氣 , 形成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個完整的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼能阻止我們去做 , 除非知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣地 , 如果我們能自動做到 , 我們會有能源供給 , 因為交通運輸會是核融合反應器和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 同樣的 , 這對人類的感官是暗的 。 但你只需要用望遠鏡 , 即使是現今的設計 , 向外看 , 你會看到相同的銀河系 , 就像我們從這裡看到的一樣 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你可以看見恆星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	你可以在當地建立粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最困難的科學會是生物領域的旅程 , 因為要花上數億年才能到達最近的生物居住的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你們 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有像生物實地之旅一樣 , 我想我們每隔幾億年就能完成一個 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	事實上 , 星系間的空間包含了所有開放式知識的前提 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何一個地方 , 都可能變成跟我們一樣的樞紐 , 如果該怎麼做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不在一個獨特的安居處 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系空間能夠創造出一個開放的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都一樣 。 地球也是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在這裡和這裡 , 並不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以知識為基礎的觀點 , 我認為應該讓我們覺得很特別 。 但它也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 若沒有必要的特定知識 , 能夠存活在宇宙的挑戰中 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超新星 , 才能在幾年後離開 , 我們都會死去 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁.雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們脆弱的書 , 從天體物理 , 到科學實驗都出錯了 , 最重要的是要用大規模毀滅性的武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會能在這個世紀生存 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他等一下會議上會談到這件事 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他這件事 , 我們可以存活下來 , 我們無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於偶然 , 而是依據我們是否創造有關時間的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險完全不是史無前例的物種會一直滅絕
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終止了 。 絕大多數的物種和文明 , 都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼我們唯一的希望就是利用一種區別我們這個物種的特徵 , 我們的文明 , 和其他物種的特徵 , 也就是 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	現在 , 讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 只是為了說明我所說的 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但根據這個理論 , 我不是一個正確的物理學家 。 在全球暖化的方面 , 我只是一個拉曼 。 一個拉曼人要做的理性是認真看待科學理論的開端 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 已經無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果我們現在最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放 , 例如京都議定書 , 其經濟活動和它極大的成本 , 成千上萬美元 , 不論是什麼 , 那就已經是個災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者的行動 , 甚至都沒有在意去解決這個問題 , 只是稍微延後它 。 所以 , 已經太遲了 , 以致於在任何人意識到危險之前 , 已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能已經太晚了 , 在1970年代 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們工業排放即將在數十億的時代中滅亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這教訓對我來說很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是說 , 我們不能永遠知道 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難 , 以及如何在災難本身的成本下解決它 , 那就不會有太多的爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預料到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的立場 , 不僅僅是麻煩 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一連串預防等於一磅解藥 , 但只有我們知道預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你在鼻子上打過鼻子 , 那麼醫學的科學並沒有教導你如何避免打孔 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治療方法 , 只專注在預防上 , 那它也無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在緩和計劃 , 將氣體排放減量 , 全部成本都減少 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計畫來降低溫度 , 且計畫要在更高的溫度上生活 , 而不是任何成本 , 而是有效率且便宜 。 有些計畫存在 , 像是在太空中的鏡子 , 將太陽光轉移開 , 鼓勵水產有機體來吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力要面對這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 我們有能力不把正確的運氣當成無限期的避免運氣 , 不只是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	用兩塊石板 , 雕刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中之一 , 卡夫: 「 問題是難以解決的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一張地毯則是: 「 問題是無可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果被困在不好的規則系統中 , 一個掙扎的國家要如何脫離貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅默提出了一個大膽的想法: 「 查特斯卡爾城市 , 市區由國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的想法是極端的:城市特區城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常吸引人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫中的一個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	讓我們給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有一個手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson能取得尖端科技 , 如手機 , 但無法取得一百歲的科技 , 讓家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	換句話說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以防止雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們能把新科技帶進來 , 讓他們可以用到像尼爾森這樣的人身上 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 它說它必須以非常低、補貼的價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 一個價格低到它銷售的每一單位都要損錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既不是資源 , 也不是獎勵 , 連接其他的使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 有可能有不同的規則 , 企業賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有獎勵要簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這類規則是nelson購買的手機公司 , 用他的電話來運作 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統知道這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電價制定的規則 , 但跑到商業和消費者的激烈抗議中 , 他們想要保存現有的補貼率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他陷入困境的規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案來協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson被困在街燈下學習 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是要試著找出如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們是否能發展出一些規則來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 我們有一項普遍抽象的見解 , 那就是 , 如果我們能提供更多的選擇給人民 , 以及在許多國家 , 領導者更多的選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導人的那種選擇 , 例如給總統用電價提高總統的選擇 , 消除經濟想要的人的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇繼續消耗補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到讓兩者更多選擇的方法 , 那就能給我們一組改變規則的規則 , 來讓我們擺脫陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	nelson也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的破壞效應 , 規則可以讓人們在黑暗中留下 , 看看美國太空總署在晚上看到的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 它就像是和鄰居相比的黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會很驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們處在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是 , 要了解北韓和南韓開始有相同的規則 , 從法律和規範的角度來看 , 同時也從更深層的角度來看 , 理解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致他們制定的規則非常不同的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變人類的規則 , 可以改變我們用來彼此互動的規則 , 做得更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在讓我們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地這裡的線上
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於它的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 大約有相同的居民數量 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相較於波多黎各 , 那裡有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則糟糕 , 因為政府實在太強壯、壓迫 , 和北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想用良好的規則來創造環境 , 我們就不能只撕裂了 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得找到方法來建立 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大大展現了與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這張圖表中 , 中國是世界上高科技領導人 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國的先驅技術 , 像是鋼、印刷、火藥 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵這些想法散播出去 , 一種利潤的動機 , 可以鼓勵散播出去 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 減緩了創新 , 把中國從世界各地移除 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 世界上其他國家創新了 , 兩者都在發展更新科技 , 同時發展更新規則 , 中國的發展已經脫離了那些進步 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入一直停滯不前 , 因為它在世界其他地方被放大了 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國平均收入的比例 , 美國平均收入的比例 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50和60年代 , 各位可以看到 , 大約有3%的人在住家 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 事情改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的經濟開始起飛 , 中國開始迅速的趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回到地圖 , 就能得到一個線索 , 讓中國的規則大幅改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的位置 , 如你所看到的 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 經營的規則和當時其他主要主要的中國規則截然不同 , 由英國管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是個地方 , 那裡有數百萬人可以從大陸開始 , 開始工作 , 比如縫衣、製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了達成增加收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致在那裡非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典範 , 領導人 , 例如香港 , 可以複製 , 當他們決定要把所有的大陸都移到市場模式上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供他人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫每個中國人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們的做法是創造出一些特殊的區域 , 在某種程度上 , 英國所做的是:讓機會去做市場規則 , 讓那些想要選擇的人可以選擇 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創建了四個特殊的經濟區 , 中國人可以來工作 , 城市很快就在那裡成長 ; 還有一些區域 , 外國公司可以進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域 , 有一個叫做 「 深圳 」 的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡有一間台台灣公司 , 製造了iphone , 在座很多人都有 , 他們用中國人的勞工來做 , 搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特區之後 , 有14個沿海地區的空地 , 最終在這些地方展現了成功 , 讓人們可以選擇進去 , 因為他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡證明了成功 , 導致了共識 , 朝向整個經濟的市場模式前進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的規模上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落的規則 , 你可以這樣做 , 但村落太小了 , 如果你有數百萬人在良好規則下工作 , 就會得到一些好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給一些人回顧 , 看看事情是怎麼發生的 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給了你機會 , 創造新的地方 , 讓人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 足以得到我們所能擁有的所有利益 , 只要有數百萬人在良好的規則下合作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是 , 我們構想了一個叫做 「 特許城市 」 的概念 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 來吸引我們所需要的所有規則 , 來吸引我們建造城市的人們 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立基礎建設──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 他們會僱用先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 那些會來到那裡的居民 , 永久地養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 為他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這一章 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一次又一次地做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些被記錄在章節裡 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	如果我們允許在未居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	從未居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以活在新的章節底下 , 但沒有人被迫活在它下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後 , 我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的選擇 , 我們需要讓各國之間合作的可能性:國家合作的情況 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先要加強市場模式 , 然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種程度上 , 英國 , 不經意地透過香港的行動 , 減少世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀我們所經歷的援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這類合作關係再次複製 , 我們就能讓全世界的規模都受惠 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到負責任的程度 , 從一個國家的控制權 , 到另一個國家 , 來掌管某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶來殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 。 但很重要的是要了解當我們開始思考這些事情時會產生的那種情感 , 能讓我們退一步 , 能夠關閉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義是不好的 , 而我們一些援助計畫中 , 反而是很糟糕的 , 就是它涉及了合作和欺騙的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇的 , 無論是領導者或是住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是對抗合作和避孕的解藥
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在實踐中演奏 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	我們拿一個特定的領導人raulcastro , 他是古巴的領導人 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定有機會為古巴做古巴 , 讓他有機會為中國做安寧 , 但他在古巴島上沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	然而 , 他在南方有一點點光 , 上面有非常特殊的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一區 , 位在南阿莫灣 , 在那裡 , 條約給美國政府負責一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去了加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , 雅諾斯有個可怕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 拿過去 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓新城市在上面建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們有個香港附近 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會回來 。 但這將會是通往現代經濟和現代世界的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還在哪裡試過呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到一個特區的概念 , 讓人們可以選擇成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們不需要強迫 , 反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更可靠的承諾 , 這種投資者會來到港口 , 建造道路 , 在新的城市裡 , 他們能做出更可靠的承諾 , 只要他們和一個夥伴合作 , 就能做出更可靠的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在一些安排中 , 有點像是一場短跑帳戶 , 把土地放在短跑帳戶中 , 伴侶國家負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	在非洲 , 也有許多土地 , 在那裡 , 新城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸邊飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的土地有著巨大的延伸 , 在那裡 , 有數十億人可以住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們將它歸納起來 , 想想 , 不僅僅是一或二個特區居住的城市 , 還有數十億個城市 , 甚至數十億人口 , 在未來一個世紀 , 會搬到城市 , 足以為他們帶來足夠的土地 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們晚上看燈 , 誤導的一件事是 , 視覺上 , 世界大部分都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我告訴各位 , 為何這不對 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以所有土地的呈現為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個正方形 , 代表地球上所有的可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被三十億人居住的城市佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 現有的城市中有30億的居民 , 佔地球上僅有3%的可耕土地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們就會像這樣點點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們將從百分之三的可耕地變成百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅減少地球上的人類足跡 , 藉由建造更多人可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則管理 , 他們可以成為城市 , 在那裡 , 人民是安全的 , 不受疾病和公共衛生的城市 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會找到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們能得到像電力這樣的基本效用 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造第一座特區城市 , 要怎麼建造它 ? 才能建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	這對手冊有幫助 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授能做的是寫一些細節 , 寫進這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不想讓我們經營城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會在野外放學術 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考像這樣的問題 , 假設不只是加拿大 , 處理拉爾卡斯特的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西也參加了西班牙 , 也許古巴也想成為四個聯合創投的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要怎麼寫條約 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有那麼先例 , 但那很容易就成功 。
how would we finance this ?	我們該如何資助呢 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們起步時 , 他們擁有的土地價值很大 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地上的收入來支付像警察、法庭等的收入 , 但學校系統和醫療系統 , 讓這個地方更吸引人 , 讓人們的收入更高 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 那些幫助建造這個區域的人的動機 , 建立它 , 建立基本規則 , 朝向正確的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓低成本、負擔得起的人在第一份工作時 , 能夠組裝類似iphone的建築物 , 但能讓那些建築物有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會掉落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	很多技術上的細節要被解決 , 但那些已經開始追求這些事的人 , 已經知道沒有障礙 , 沒有障礙 , 除了想像的失敗之外 , 其它方式 , 會讓我們無法實現真正的全球雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能成功 , 是因為地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和別人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 共享意味著我們每個人都能得到較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那樣的方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:管理我們如何互動的規則 ; 例如 , 讓我們有一個計程系統 , 來支持一項研究大學 , 免費提供某種知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	我們有一個系統 , 讓土地能登記在政府辦公室 , 人民可以承認承諾是殖民地 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能持續創新我們對規則的空間 , 尤其是創新 , 想出改變規則的概念 , 所以我們不會被困在不好的規則 , 那麼我們就能繼續前進 , 真正讓世界變得更美好 , 像納爾遜和他的朋友不再需要在路燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學先驅克雷格•凡特需要休息一下他的史詩般的圓環探險 , 來談談他的團隊發現的數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 來繪製海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海上 , 和克萊格•凡特 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時間 , 我被幾個人問到我關於老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者大大勝過悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我將告訴各位 , 我們將如何從基因編碼轉換到開始寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	直到十年前 , 我們才出版了第一組免費的有機體序列 , 也就是大象流感 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月的基因組計畫 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八小時內做同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加上:大部份的人類病原體、幾株植物、昆蟲和哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十年前 , 在這個想法的階段 , 基因組學在今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因序列 , 數百個 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	今年我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金得到了一百三十個基因組的補助 , 作為環境生物的一面 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因密碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 正如我們所看到的 , 我們幾乎無法在這個星球上找到可用的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人都不知道 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成了地球生物質的一半 , 而所有的動物只佔所有生物總量的一分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許牛津的人們通常不會做的事 , 但如果你把它放到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升都有大約一百萬個細菌 , 和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到五千種微生物物種在兩年前被特徵了 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開啟了sercer二次探險 , 當時我們正處於大海攝影探險 , 嘗試每200英哩的海洋樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始測試 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉帕戈斯 , 穿越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這非常困難 ; 我們在航海船上做這件事 , 有部分是要協助刺激年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只用海水過濾它 , 我們用不同的濾器收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 每24小時就可以排列出一億個基因編碼的字母 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉此 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 認為我們眼睛裡的視覺色素只有一到兩種有機體有著同樣的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有海洋上半部的生物 , 都擁有相同的光電接收器 , 並使用陽光 , 就像它們的能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個網站 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 和50 , 000種新物種一樣多 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在將它延伸到空中 , 給sloan基金會的獎金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量我們每天呼吸的病毒和細菌數量 , 特別是在飛機上或隔離室 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的外表過濾 ; 我們一天從紐約市的建築物上收集了十億微生物的數量 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於當下的定序過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在數據收集方面 , 我們在加拉帕戈斯所在的地方 , 我們發現幾乎每200英哩 , 我們在海洋中看到巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合理的 , 以不同溫度的梯度來看 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 以紅色溫度為基礎 , 藍色是溫暖 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一點讓我們感到驚訝的是這些光受器偵測不同的光波長我們可以根據它們的胺基酸序列來預測
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些從各個地區轉變為區域 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外地 , 在深海 , 大部分是藍色的 , 光受器通常會看見藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們可能更加不同 , 在極端的紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了得到一個評估我們的基因複製品 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們在探險的範圍之外 , 這代表了地球上所有基因資料的一半 , 總共大約兩千九百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些資料放入基因家庭 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬名主要的基因家庭 , 但我們在環境中所採集的每一種新樣本 , 都會增加給這些新家庭的線性時尚 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於這個星球上基礎基因、元件和生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看所謂的進化樹 , 我們在右上角和動物的右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩億九千萬個基因中 , 我們的基因體中只有大約兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物集合在一起 , 我們可能有不到三萬個 , 可能有十幾個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因不僅僅是演化的設計成分 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在基因中心的觀點也許回到理查德•達金斯的觀點 , 遠超過基因中心的觀點 , 這些基因組成的構造不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年或二十年間 , dna定序的速度和dna定序的速度差不多 , 且變得很快 , 且很便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學 , 當我們在1995年重組第二組基因組時 , 最初想到的就是墨西哥柏斯的生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只想問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 是否有較小的基因組組可以組成最小的營運系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉移 , 突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉換器只是隨機插入基因碼中的小片dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們插入基因的中間 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張基因圖 , 可以用轉移插入的地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 正面基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境是非常關鍵的 , 你只能根據環境到底是什麼來定義一個必要或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智力方法和13個相關的有機體基因組做比較 , 我們試著去比較它們的共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們發現這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因和所有13個有機體相同 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	池塘擴張一點 , 如果我們忽略一個細胞寄生蟲 , 它會擴展得更廣 , 當我們觀察核心基因的核心組合 , 大約310組 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以 , 我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 取決於你的觀點 , 至於500年最低的300到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是建造一個人造染色體 , 裡面有這些基因 , 我們得要用以現場為基礎的時尚來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大片中合成精確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	漢姆.史密斯和clydehutchison , 我的同事開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們可以在兩週內合成一個五千個鹼基對病毒 , 準確度是百分之百精確的 , 以其序列和生物學來說 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個相當令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始開著病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒--一個小兒麻痺病毒在一年之前被製造出來 , 但它只有一個活躍的十三年 , 且要做三年 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體製造自己的硬體 , 那就是我們對生物學的觀念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻開始關心生態戰爭 , 我最近在參議院委員會前有證詞 , 美國政府設立了特殊委員會來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要記住現實是很重要的 , 而不是人們的想像力會發生什麼事 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今的任何病毒都可以被基因組定序 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就對伊波拉或天花的事物感到害怕 , 但這種生物的dna沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造了天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正關心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 努力創造生物武器代理人 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這份研究真的被遺漏了 , 未來應該就沒有任何的知識來製造設計病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為兩年內就有可能實現單細胞生物 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能在十年內 , 那些我們擁有的真菌細胞 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變人造染色體的貓咪和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 你要如何把所有其他人都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組系統 , 將它們重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體中衍生出來的 , 失序的無線電 , 可以用三百萬個輻射 , 而不是被殺 。
