it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆炸後 , 它會重新組合它的基因組 , 大約12到24小時後 , 它的染色體被拆開了 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種有機體在地球上無所不在 , 可能是因為我們旅行到外太空的存在 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是在約五十萬輻射後的玻璃貝克 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 而微生物就坐在底部 , 變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際發生的圖片 , 上面的圖片顯示了一百七十萬張輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的分開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重組 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的令人驚訝的是這些有機體能做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種 , 如果不是數萬種 , 在這個星球上有能力做到這一點的物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此 , 我們認為合成細胞將會有很大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還有希望環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們排序的第三個有機體中 , 它住在沸騰的水溫下 , 它的能量來源是氫 , 它的碳來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 成千上萬的不同有機體從二氧化碳中存活下來 , 並捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其使用石油合成過程的碳 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物體 , 住在一氧化碳中 , 我們用它來減少水分裂 , 來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有許多可以改造代謝甲烷的途徑 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一個重大的計畫 , 用挪威的雕像來捕捉並把甲烷從那裡轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短時間內 , 我認為將有一個新的領域叫做 「 組合基因組 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些大量的基因組修復和同源的組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可以製造一百萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 就如同所有的生物學而言 , 你在篩選 , 不論你在篩選氫化生產 , 或化學生產 , 或單純的可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的角色 , 會很棒 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 從陽光直接製造氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用被氧氣調節 , 我們有一種氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了細胞膜 , 分解複雜糖的酵素 , 分解成簡單糖和發酵 , 在同一個細胞中產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在大型實驗室使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學物質比我們最好的化合物能產生的還要複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境復原的來源 , 也可能替換了石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來結束 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年延遲實驗的開端 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 來嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖把他們的經文當作法律書 , 他們找不到任何禁止創造生命的任何東西 , 所以這一定是可以的 。 唯一的疑慮是生物戰事方面 , 但給了我們前進的主意 , 以我們做這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會剛資助了多重機構的研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和益處 , 以及像我這樣的科學團隊應該要在這個領域中使用的規則 , 我們正試著設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們能否設計東西來製造乾淨能源 , 或許改革開發中國家能做些什麼 , 並提供各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說幸福和成功根深蒂固的特質:我們對過去、現在、未來的方向 。 他建議我們在未來的第一步改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理學、科學、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了個健康的處方 , 花了很長的時間 ,
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的概念 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘 。 三十秒鐘的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	讓它安靜下來 , 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間 , 終結序列 , 一試 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普•辛巴多:咱們來談談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 拜託 , 不要太小心了 。 請小心 。 」 「 我做了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 , 別拋棄eve 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 一口 。 到底是什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑的 。 重點是產出、抗拒 , 是的 , 後來 , 衝動性、反思性、焦點 , 以及未來焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	被承諾的美德落在當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少女在婚前宣揚性別缺席和處女的青少年 , 感謝喬治•布希多半 , 60% , 被性誘惑所吸引 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都沒有用出生控制權 。
so much for promises .	承諾太多了 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們誘惑四歲的孩子 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗者回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 它會支付 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子因誘惑而放棄 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 當然 , 其他的 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 現在延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	華特•米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 14年後 , 試圖發現那些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 抗拒的孩子和受益的孩子之間有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些拒絕分數250分的人 , 在座位上比較高 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這太龐大了 。 這就像一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且有決心的 。 今天對我而言 , 關鍵在於 , 他們是未來的 , 而不是全面性的 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間的觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你的人類經驗分成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	你自動做 , 無意識地做這件事 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、社會階級、教育程度之間的差異不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們可以變得有偏見 , 因為你學會了濫用其中的一些 , 並且濫用其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出一個決定 , 你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人而言 , 只有在當下的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你在感受什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	那些人 , 當他們做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說: 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱這些人為 「 偽造 」 , 因為他們專注於什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是針對預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來 」 。 他們的焦點是 「 未來 」 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想主張時間觀點的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全不知道的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有這種偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	嗯 , 其實有六種方式 。 有兩種方式可以呈現出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以修正 , 兩種未來的方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在過度積極或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是具體的 , 也就是你把焦點放在生活的喜悅 , 或當前主義者──不重要 , 你的人生被控制著 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以有未來的目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:生命起源於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維靈活度 , 讓時間觀點流暢地取決於情況的需求 , 這就是你必須學習的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	很快地 , 最佳時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	在過去的高度 , 在未來的高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	而在現代主義上調節 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和實在主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的顳葉混合是你從過去過去所得到的 , 給了你根 。 你連結你的家人、身分和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來所得到的 , 是翅膀到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的就是能量 , 去探索你自己 , 地方 , 人們 , 感知 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間看過多的觀點 , 都會比正面的觀點更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來如何犧牲成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 他們犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲有趣的時光 , 犧牲個人的絕緣 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 , 影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為了工作、成就和控制而活著 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信這和一些ted人有所共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我有共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯貧民區長大 , 一個西西西里家庭 , 所有人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來到這裡 , 作為一個長久以來的人 , 他們做這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我有未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那塊棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你拿到兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了現代主義 , 我把焦點放在過去的思維上 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有生產力 , 且我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用到許多世界問題上:改變輟學率 , 結合成癮 , 增加青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治療創傷後壓力症候群 , 讓 「 永續 」 和 「 保育 」 , 減少身體復健 , 在那裡有50%的輟學率 , 改變了自殺恐怖份子 , 以及改變家庭衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以我想以此作結:許多人生的謎題可以透過了解時間觀和其他人的觀點來解答 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深奧 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今的頭條在一百年內會很重要 ? 一百年後 ? kirkcron的 「 長新聞 」 計畫收集了現今很重要的故事 , 數十年來 , 甚至會有共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調了我們未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcron:現在 , 真正的消息是 ,
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞中淹沒 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社每年就有三百五十萬個新聞 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來看 , 那些故事中有多少會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是長期新聞的主意 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是長期的基金會 , 是由tedster所創立的 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華•布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們正在尋找的新聞故事 , 可能是從現在起五十到十萬年後 , 可能仍然重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你看新聞過濾器時 , 很多東西會從旁邊掉下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 為了從a.p.上述的故事 , 這會在十年內發生嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會發生什麼事嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 過去一年的上述故事是經濟 , 我很快就打賭 , 這種衰退將會是古老的消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 未來有什麼樣的故事會造成什麼樣的改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 咱們來談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液循環 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 某一天就在這裡 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近有些故事:奈米蜜蜂和真實蜜蜂毒液的腫瘤 , 它們會把基因送到大腦中 ; 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	那麼資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在有六十億人在吃麻煩 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國會餓死 , 沒有基因改造的作物 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲已經賭注了十億人 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會非常不一樣 , 如果中國設定議程 , 他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們過度推翻了美國 , 成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們超越了德國 , 成為最大的出口國 , 他們開始做dna測驗 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各式各樣的方式來推動我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近的一些發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 現在已經散播到每一個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自主導導導向的機器人科學家很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命也可能不再需要我們了 ; 一根微生物在十二萬年後會醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎沒有我們 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但 , 去年我在月球上找到了水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓這個蟻群更容易放上去 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署沒有做到 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某人可能會寫一份大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長期來看 , 有些新聞比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家卡羅琳•波科斯從卡西尼航行到土星的影像 , 專注於它最大的衛星、泰坦 , 以及佛洛茲.羅德斯 , 這似乎是冰中的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化視覺化、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡羅琳•波科讓我們飛到土星上 ,
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘 , 我會帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這趟旅程 , 各位和我已經經歷了很多年 , 大約50年前 , 人類第一次離開地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅僅是真的在月球上設定了腳 , 我們已經把機械太空船分散到所有行星上 , 全部八個行星上 , 我們已經降落在小行星上 , 在這個時點 , 我們有了一艘太空船 , 用來冥王星 , 前人稱它為行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟航行 , 去了解某樣東西 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球 , 我們的地球 , 以及我們的生活 , 來臨 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中的所有地方 , 我們可能會去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 這是土星 。 我們去過土星 , 在1980年代早期 , 探訪土星時 , 我們調查土星的細節已經變得更加深刻 , 因為卡西尼號太空船 , 在2004年夏天 , 穿越了星際空間 , 在2004年的夏天 , 環繞土星軌道 , 成為了人類最遙遠的機器人 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是很豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 顯然擴張超越了這個系統的調查 , 已經達到了巨大的宇宙範圍 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就知道很多恆星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張很漂亮的照片 , 這張照片是我們最接近的銀河系 , 最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	然後 , 這裡有一個美麗的旋pool銀河系是由哈伯太空望遠鏡所組成 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程其實是一部分 , 也是人類旅程的比喻 , 來了解我們身邊的事物之間的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入這張圖片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	讓我痛苦的是 , 我無法告訴你們 , 我們在卡西尼學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法給你們看我們過去兩年半所拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我要專注在這個重大的探險探險旅程中 , 其中兩個最令人興奮的故事 , 就是我們正在進行土星旅行的旅程 , 過去兩年半 , 一直都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星是由非常大且多樣化的衛星組成的 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的尺寸從幾公里長 , 大到和美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝土星的大部分美麗的照片 , 事實上 , 土星與它的一些衛星相伴 。 這是土星和鑽石土星 , 接著 , 這是土星展示了地表的環狀壁虎 , 展示了它們的垂直稀薄度 , 和土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星47顆衛星中有兩個是排名 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	那些是土衛六和土衛二 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼抵達那裡 , 是太陽系中我們剩下最多未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	而這個身體有很長一段感興趣的人觀看了這個星球 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常厚 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像是地球上的環境 , 或者至少在過去 , 比太陽系中的任何其他身體都要大 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是分子氮氣 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸一樣 , 但它的大氣層卻充滿了像甲烷、丙烷和乙烷的簡單有機物質 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在土衛六大氣層中高度被打破 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 形成了 「 黑色粒子 」 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這隻海鮮無所不在 , 完全是全球性的 , 也是霸主 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你不能用眼睛在光譜中可見的區域看到我們的表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些觸覺粒子在我們和卡西尼一起到達之前 , 已經有數十億年了 , 溫柔地漂移到表面 , 將表面覆蓋在有機泥中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以 , 就像泰坦等同於焦油 , 油 , 或我們不知道的 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們猜想的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 可能是土衛六表面溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是要把水送到地球上 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	在大氣層中 , 它是可以被凝聚的 , 所以認知到這個情況 , 帶到一個怪異的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在這些雲層上 , 上方有數百公里的霧氣 , 防止任何陽光照射到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管寒冷 , 土衛六的表面下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上雨是如何在地球上運作的:它雕刻了石頭 ; 它形成了河流和開車 ; 它可以創造峽谷 ; 它可以在大盆地和隕石坑中聚集 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥土洗掉高山頂和山丘 , 洗到低地 。 停下來 , 想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	黑暗 。 鐵達尼號的高低點和地球上深處的地震一樣黑 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很噁心 , 很悲慘 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能站在密西根湖邊邊 , 用油漆薄板來模仿 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們和卡西尼一起到達那裡之前的土衛六表面 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在土衛六所發現的 , 雖然細節不一樣 , 比那個故事更吸引人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼人一樣──它就像是一位陪審團的冒險 , 實現了 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是titan , 背著太陽 , 圈圈是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	還有另一顆衛星 , 我甚至不知道它是哪個 。 它是非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器可以透過大氣層看到海面 , 我的攝影機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮又黑暗的區域 , 這跟我們目前為止一樣 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在是太神奇了:我們無法找出我們在泰坦看到的是什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細觀察這個區域時 , 你會開始看到我們不知道的無數通道 。 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 事實上 , 一個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面上有很少的隕石坑 , 意思是 , 土衛六的表面很年輕 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像是地形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來就像被拉開一樣 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到一個星球上的線性 , 就表示已經有破裂 , 像個錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經有了直覺的改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一件事件 , 許多人都被視為是卡西尼對土衛六的高度調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這就是呼吸探測器的部署 , 歐洲的呼吸探測器 , 卡西尼在太陽系上載了七年 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了2.5小時才能下降 , 直到表面上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這個事件的重要性 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這個裝置是人類製造的 , 它第一次在人類歷史上降落在外太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我看來 , 這件事非常顯著 , 這事件應該要和美國和歐洲的每個城市的陳腔帶遊行一起慶祝 , 不幸的是 , 這並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另外一個原因 。 這是個國際的使命 , 在德國 , 舉辦的活動是英國口音、美國口音、德國口音、法語、義大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是一個關於 「 聯合國 」 所謂的 「 聯合國 」 的示範:一個真正的聯合國 , 加入一個極為好的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 探索一個星球是很大的 , 漸漸了解一個行星系統 , 對於所有人類歷史來說 , 這個行星系統是不可思議的 , 現在人類已經觸碰了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我開始談起雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是非常激動的事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器在下面進行大氣層測量 , 也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 看到探測器表面的第一張圖片是泰坦的表面 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真的很震驚 , 因為我們希望其他的照片都能從軌道上拍下來 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是一種不明確的模式 , 一種地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種只由液體流動而形成的趨勢 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以遵循這些通道 , 你可以看到它們是如何聚集在一起的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們把這條通道連接到這裡 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍攝的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是8公里的照片 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里大概是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要穿越美國的飛機旅行 , 你會飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是泰坦航空的窗戶 , 飛越土衛六的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在表面休息 , 我要展示給你們看 , 各位先生女士 , 第一張從外太陽系的月亮表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰塊 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它降落在其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 且它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以我們降落的不是液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器基本上就是土衛六的平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個沒有安慰的土地 , 充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是因為這種材料已經從土衛六的高地上清洗掉 , 穿過我們看到的這些管道 , 且已經耗盡了數十億年 , 來填滿低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是海吉探測器登陸的原因 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然在我們的影像中沒有標誌 , 甚至在熱量的影像中 , 沒有任何大型的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 會變得更困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六赤道地區的電影 , 顯示這些沙丘高達一百公尺高 , 分離了幾公里 , 它們延伸了幾英里和里程數 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	數百英里高達一千到一千兩百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很顯然 , 這是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	再一次 , 令人困惑的是沒有液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到北極地區的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在土衛六南極地的南極地區有一個湖泊 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是安大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛越了土衛六北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了像卡西亞海的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎這些液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節 , 都顯然是土衛六極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們找到泰坦是個很了不起、很神秘的地方 。 它很奇怪 , 但卻是外星人 , 但有著像地球一樣的地質形態 , 也有很棒的地理多樣性 , 一個很棒的世界 , 在太陽系中 , 只有太陽系的複雜性和豐富性才是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是個小月球 , 土衛六大小約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到在英格蘭旁邊 , 只為了讓你看到大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 非常明亮 , 它的表面很明顯地被破裂 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個非常地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二的母親在南極發現了新發現 , 我們正在看南極 , 在那裡我們找到了破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是被覆蓋的 。 這些碎片是用有機材料覆蓋的 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個區域 , 整個南極地區 , 都升高了溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 發現地球上的南極比熱帶更熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍了額外的圖片 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片中發現 , 冰粒會將數百英哩延伸到太空中 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張圖描繪出來時 , 我們會看到這些噴射機餵食了一加水 , 事實上 , 在其他的圖像中 , 在土衛二上方數千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我的團隊和我研究了像這樣的圖片 , 像這個 , 思考了卡西尼其他的結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射機可能從土衛二表面下噴發液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們可能有液態水、有機材料和過多的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 也就是說 , 一個適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中發現了生命 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明基因的發生不只一次 , 而是在我們的太陽系中 , 獨立發生兩次 , 那就意味著 , 根據推論 , 它在宇宙中發生了很驚人的次數 , 且它有137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球也是我們所知唯一的行星 , 就是充滿生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 我們唯一認識的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有任何人在1960年代時 , 都原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 那你會記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球是從太空拍攝出來的 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有著巨大的影響 , 我們對地球的保護有責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼首次拍了一幅相當於人類以前從未見過的照片
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全食 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張不太美麗的圖片中 , 你可以看到由太陽所組成的主要環 , 你可以看到太陽重新折射的影像 , 你可以看到這個環 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的排放 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但就好像那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中發現 , 看見我們自己的星球 , 在土星光環的手臂上爬上 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 我們有一些深刻的動作 , 可以從外遇看到我們自己 , 捕捉到我們的小藍色的星球 , 在其他星球的天空中 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們從中獲益的這個觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個半個世紀前開始的發現旅程中得到最好的獎賞 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	在2005年 , 只有15%的世界被繪製出來 。 這慢慢地在災難後 , 隱藏了未經使用的土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 在這短短的演講中 , google的卡特加達展示地圖 , 全球各地的一群人繪製的地圖工具 , 用於繪製他們的世界地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	最近的卡特加達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 , 建立經濟體系 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 颶風納利斯遭到毀滅性的緬甸人 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人需要協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人和供應到該地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法幫助到cyclone受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信 , 在2005年 , 世界上只有15%被描繪成地理的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國投入了世界上大部分人臉龐的問題:沒有細節地圖 。
but help was coming .	但救援已經來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40名志工用了一套新的軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路、三千間醫院、物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體 ? google繪圖機 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	google地圖製造商是一項技術 , 讓我們每個人都能繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製每樣東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 影片商店到轉角店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名赫南多•索托承認 , 對大部分開發中國家而言 , 經濟升降的關鍵是要處理大量未經調整的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 僅僅在印度 , 一兆美元的房地產仍然未被啟發 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 在170個國家 , 數以千計的使用者就繪製了數百萬個資訊 , 創造了一幅細節的地圖 , 從來沒有被認為是可行的 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這使得熱情使用者的力量無所不在 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在讓我們來看看一些使用者所創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 正如我們所說 , 在這170個國家 , 人們正在繪製世界的地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家更近 , chalua , 班加羅爾的g.g.路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何、手勢識別和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以百計城市使用者的勝利 , 一個使用者 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們未開發的地球70%的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落布德魯斯在十個月大的非暴力抗議活動中阻止一道障礙在他們的橄欖樹上被建造出來 。 你有聽過嗎 ? 巴西製片人約利亞.朱利亞.巴哈亞問為什麼我們只關注以色列衝突的暴力 , 而不是非暴力的領導人 , 有一天會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:注意非暴力的注意 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦人的工作 , 他們試圖用和平的手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我和歐洲及美國的作品一起旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我常常從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了很多時間拍攝數十名巴勒斯坦人 , 他們使用非暴力來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人正試著要打造一個全國性的非暴力運動 , 終止職業 , 並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 在座大部分人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	國外發生了什麼事和國外感知之間的分歧是為何我們尚未有巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動成功的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	我今天在這裡要談的是注意力的力量 , 你的注意力 , 以及在西岸、加薩和其他地方的非暴力運動的崛起和發展 , 但今天 , 我的案件研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 最少缺少非暴力來成長的 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經存在的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用布德魯斯帶你到這個叫布德魯斯的村子來說明這個點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建造一個隔離障礙 , 其中一部分的障礙會在村落上蓋 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被包圍 , 所以他們會失去自由的權利 , 到其他的西岸 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地領導者的靈感 , 他們發起了和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們有一種感覺 , 在地面上看起來是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知牆會和以色列分開巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現牆會偷我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:柵欄事實上 , 為恐怖創造了一個解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男人:今天你被邀請參加和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你加入了數十個以色列兄弟姐妹 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列行動主義者:沒有什麼比非暴力反對者更嚇人 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有人能那樣做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔•派對成員:我們必須忽略傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯•派對:我們是完整的和諧 , 我們想要把它散播到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	聊天:聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔、哈馬斯和流行的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:柵欄的凝塊持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就好像在世界各地射擊 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列行動主義者:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊還有其他人 , 甚至不是牛仔 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止伊斯蘭國 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	蛋白:這是一場和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	溝通:我們能做到 ! 我們能做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴查亞:我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體並沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 , 在2003年發生 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 經過10個月的和平抗爭 , 說服以色列政府將土地上的障礙移到綠線上 , 也就是國際認可以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抗爭自從散播到整個西岸的村莊 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦鄰里 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然沉默於這些故事中 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會造成很深刻的後果 , 造成非暴力的可能性 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦的存活 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有著非常重要的共通點 , 兩者都有形式的劇院尋求觀眾的理想 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷地收到頭版 , 並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦的議題 , 那對非暴力的領導者來說 , 要對他們的社區來說 , 公民不服從是可行的選擇 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對在座的父母來說是毫無意外的 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子更大聲地投擲你的孩子 , 最好的方式就是讓他第一次關注他 , 他把手放進去 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	螞蟻會變成兒時心理學家所謂的 「 功能性行為 」 , 因為孩子們知道他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以鼓勵或貶低行為 , 只要給予或讓孩子們注意力就好了 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以被影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇把注意力放在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東的衝突 , 帶來和平的核心是要將非暴力行為轉化為功能性行為 , 讓更多關注現今在地面上的非暴力領袖 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝西岸、加薩和東耶路撒冷的村落中 , 我看到即使是一部紀錄片 , 也會影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉賈的村子裡 , 離耶路撒冷很近 , 社區正面臨著和布德魯斯非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去很多土地 , 沒有任何可取得的自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力 , 但從沒人注意到他們就越來越不滿了 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好的示範和最明確的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民看到布德魯斯在電影中記錄了布德魯斯的故事 , 認為確實有人在追蹤他們在做的事 , 有人在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做索麗達里ot , 意思是希伯來的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者一直把布德魯斯當作主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列人從來沒有活躍過 , 看電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華拉賈和索里達里德運動的例子顯示 , 即使是一部小預算的獨立電影 , 也可以扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力行為轉化為功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週非暴力的示威 , 在村落中發生 , 比如比利、尼、瓦拉、耶路撒冷 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 如希克•賈拉和史瓦 , 非暴力的領導人 , 在他們的工作中 , 會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像它們從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見識過 , 如果我們做到了 , 他們就會乘上去 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果它們的數量會增加 , 它們的影響力會在以色列的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力終於可以解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明非暴力在布德魯斯之類的地方是有效的 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們關注他們 , 讓他們可以證明它在各地運作 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•辛克有個簡單但有力的模式 , 鼓舞人心的領導人 , 都從金圈開始 , 問題是: 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德金 , 以及萊特兄弟 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售 , 賣 , 成功 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•桑德克:偉大的領導者啟發了行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不像我們假設的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能夠做到似乎違反所有假設時 , 你要如何解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 一年又一年 , 他們比他們所有的競爭都要有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才華、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼 , 為什麼他們似乎有不同之處 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金恩帶領民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是那天最偉大的演說者 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟們能夠想出控制權 , 強權的人飛行 , 當然還有其他更好的隊伍 , 更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有完成人類飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的玩法 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這項發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的方式 , 它甚至深深地改變了我運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁路德金 , 或是他們認為的萊特兄弟 , 採取行動 , 並以相同的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是編碼它 , 可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠鼓舞其他人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是怎麼做到的 , 不管你稱之為 「 分化價值觀 」 的提案 , 不管你稱之為 「 適當的程序 」 或 「 適當的程序 」 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做他們要做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 , 我不是要 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 一直都是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	我指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎呢 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	因此 , 我們思考的方式、行動方式、溝通的方式 , 都來自外面 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 。 我們從最清楚的事物到最模糊的事物 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵人心的領導人和激勵人心的組織 , 不論他們的規模 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 採取行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為它們很容易了解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息聽起來會像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 可以使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷是這樣做的 , 大部分的銷售都是這樣做的 , 那就是我們大多數人之間的溝通方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做的事 , 我們說我們是如何變得更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票 , 諸如此類 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師 , 有最大的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很棒的氣體流程 , 它有皮革座位 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果電腦是如何溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是 , 把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 可以使用和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好是用電腦做好的 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同的是吧 ? 你準備好要跟我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明了人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼要做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都很自在地買蘋果電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很自在地買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的電話 , 或是蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼可以區別它們的競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都一樣有資格做這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway發表了平面電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們非常有資格製作平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在製作平面螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	德爾想出了mp3播放器和pdas , 他們製造了很棒的品質產品 , 他們能做出完美的設計產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到這件事 , 我們甚至無法想像從現場購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從電腦公司買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要跟你所擁有的所有人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我要告訴你的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	這一切都基於生物學的基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看看人類大腦的橫軸 , 從上往下看 , 你可以看到人類的大腦實際上被分成三個主要元件 , 與黃金圈完全相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 與 「 什麼 」 層面相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析思考和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有決策 , 它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面的溝通 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們從內部傳遞訊息時 , 我們直接對控制行為的大腦說話 , 接著 , 我們允許人們將它合理化 , 用我們說和做的事 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候你會給某人所有的事實和數據 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說了什麼 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用這個動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的大腦部位無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好能忍受的就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你會說你是帶著你的心 , 或是你的靈魂領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭把它打破 , 不是其他身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中 , 控制決策的那部分 , 而非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼要做你做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼要做你做的事 , 那你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你的人 , 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你雇用人 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人 , 他們會用血汗和淚水來工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有什麼比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀初期 , 追求人類飛行的追求 , 就像是那天的網路com 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley所擁有的 , 我們假設成功的食譜 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 甚至現在 , 你問人們: 「 你的產品或你的公司為什麼會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給予你相同的三件事:不受啟發、錯誤的人、壞的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	一直都是同樣的三件事 , 讓我們來探究一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美金 , 由戰爭部門來想出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢根本沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦了一座座位 , 在史密森尼工作 , 當時非常有連結 ; 他知道當時的所有大心 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的心態金錢 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報隨處跟著他 , 每個人都在為拉ngley開根 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	我們怎麼可能從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠在俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的食譜 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們用自行車店的腳踏車來支付夢想 ; 沒有一個人在萊特兄弟的團隊中受過大學教育 , 甚至是奧維爾或威爾堡 ; 紐約時報跟隨他們到處走 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾堡被一個目的、一個目的、一個目的、一個信念所驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這台飛行機器 , 就會改變世界的軌跡 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要變得富有 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	注意 , 看看發生了什麼事
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想 , 和他們一起工作 , 血汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另外一些人只是為薪水工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們講述故事 , 每次萊特兄弟出櫃時 , 他們會需要花五組零件 , 因為他們會在他們進來之前撞到幾次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟飛了起來 , 沒有人去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們就發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明 , 蘭利被錯誤的動機驅使:萊特兄弟飛行的那天 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 那是很棒的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人是很重要的 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做 「 創新的擴散法則 」 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	人口的前2.5%是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%是我們的早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你最早的大多數人 , 你的大多數人和拉克人 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人購買觸覺電話的唯一原因 , 就是你不再買輪車電話 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都處在不同時間點 , 但創新的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受這個想法 , 你就無法做到這個臨界點 , 直到你達成了15%到18%的市場滲透 , 然後系統的尖端 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你: 「 喔 , 這大約是10% 。 」 很驕傲地 ,
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以超過百分之十的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們大約有百分之十的人只是 「 了解 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	就像那種直覺的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到那些在你做生意之前找到的 , 而不是那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 在這裡 , 你必須關閉的這個小差距 , 如同jeffreymoore所說的 , " 跨越這個隔閡 " , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大部分的人都不會嘗試一些東西 , 直到有人先試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們很自在地做出這些直覺決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更自在地做出那些直覺的決策 , 由他們對世界的信念所驅動 , 而不只是產品可用 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人是排隊排隊六個小時買iphone的人 , 當他們第一次出櫃時 , 可以在下星期走進店裡 , 買下一台手機 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人一開始就花了四萬美金在平面電視上 , 儘管這項技術是次等的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們並沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己也做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	那是因為他們想要成為第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 你做的就是證明你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	前六個小時 , 人們買iphone的原因 , 站在前六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們希望每個人看到的:他們是第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗和一個有名的成功 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 知名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說的 , 第二 , 成功的秘訣是金錢、對的人、對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八、九年前 , tivo出版到現在 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受歡迎 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我常在垃圾時間華納dvr上講tivo東西 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是個商業上的失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是30或40美元 , 然後被壓倒 , 結果從來沒有在10美元以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它在六歲以上的交易 , 除了幾條小插頭之外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個可以暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過商業廣告 , 回收現場的電視節目 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 你甚至不會問你 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗大多說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡全面控制的人 , 天哪 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視、跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心 , 去聽金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有發出任何邀請 , 沒有網站來檢查日期 。
how do you do that ?	你該怎麼做 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是唯一在美國受過早期權利的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們 , 美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走動 , 告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的原因的人 , 讓他成為自己 , 告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人知道這個詞 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	有25萬人在右天出現在對的時間聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人來找他 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們相信的美國 , 讓他們在一輛巴士旅行八小時 , 站在華盛頓的太陽中 , 站在八月中期 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世上有兩種法律:由更高的權威和由人類所組成的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有由人類所制定的法律都和較高權威制定的法律一致 , 否則我們生活在一個正義的世界裡 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好 , 民權運動是最完美的 , 協助他把他的成因帶到生命中 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟著 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在 , 聽政治人物們 , 他們的全面12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有啟發任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領袖 , 有領袖 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些領導人激勵我們的人 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們遵循領導者 , 不是因為我們需要 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導者 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 他們有能力激發他們周圍的人 , 或找到啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你在哪裡停車 ? 你怎麼知道你是不是在正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家尼爾•尼爾研究我們周圍的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結到記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾•布爾斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你身在何處 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大停車場時 , 我們要如何記住我們停車的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	問題來了荷馬 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 黃色標示的是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那裡受損 , 就像阿茲海默症一樣 , 你無法記住你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是拉丁文 , 名字是 「 海馬 」 , 相似之處 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其他部分 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
