and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元互相溝通 , 藉由發送小脈衝或脈衝電流 , 透過連結彼此 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成 , 它們非常緊密相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠在覓食或探索環境中尋找食物的個別神經元 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像一下 , 我們正在紀錄這隻老鼠的海馬體中的一個神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發射電流時 , 會有一個紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到的是 , 這個神經元知道當老鼠在牠的環境中進入一個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	大腦其他部位會透過發送電衝刺來傳遞訊號 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以顯示神經元的激發率 , 作為動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從不同神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物在其環境的不同部分時 , 不同的神經元會發射 , 就像這個正方形的盒子 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起組成一張地圖 , 讓大腦不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	地點細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人在玩電玩遊戲 , 他們開車繞著一個小鎮 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體內的細胞會被激發 , 會被活躍起來 , 每當他們開車經過一個特定的地點 , 就會開始發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個位置細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人的環境在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	最上方的那隻 , 像是在老鼠的箱子牆上發射的中間 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴張盒子時 , 發射地點會擴張 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的一面 , 每當有一面牆接近南邊時 , 就會有一面牆 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放在盒子裡 , 細胞會在兩個地方被激發 , 不論在哪裡 , 都會有一面牆到南邊 , 當動物在盒子裡探索時 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這預測了 , 感測到你周圍的邊界方向和邊界方向 , 對海馬迴來說 , 尤其重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬迴的輸入中 , 細胞會被發現 , 在海馬迴中 , 它會對偵測邊界或邊緣的反應 , 特別是從老鼠或老鼠的方向 , 來偵測 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近一面牆 , 或東邊的邊界時 , 不論是方形的邊緣 , 或圓形的牆 , 或是圓形的邊緣 , 甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物會跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發射當南邊有邊界時 , 不論是桌邊的邊緣 , 或牆壁 , 甚至是兩張桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	因此 , 我們認為位置細胞會決定動物在哪裡探索 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物體在哪裡 , 比如這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的汽車在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常它們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和尺寸 , 就像我們用位置細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個例子中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟在哪裡被改變 , 因為你如何改變環境的形狀和尺寸 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小方形的環境中 , 然後如果你問別人它在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變得更大 , 他們認為旗幟已經被伸展到完全相同的地方 , 位置細胞發射出來 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你還記得旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存你位置細胞的位置 , 這樣你就可以回歸到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以最符合你位置細胞的激發模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那引導你回到你想要記得的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在哪裡進行動作 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們採取一些外在的路徑 , 也許我們停了一下 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以整合這條路徑 , 大約是前進的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也得到這種整合路徑 , 來自一種叫做網格細胞的細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞在海馬體輸入的輸入中 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每一個細胞都會在一系列不同的地點在整個環境中發射 , 以驚人的三角形格子在整個環境中發射 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從不同顏色的數個網格細胞中記錄 , 每個圖案都有類似發射的圖案 , 每個細胞的格狀圖案都和其他細胞有稍微相似 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以這個網格上的紅色部份和綠色的這個 , 和這個上面的藍色 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 這就像老鼠可以把一個虛擬的網格放到整個環境中 , 有點像你在地圖上看到的緯度和長度線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的位置 , 這樣它就可以利用它自己的動作來知道它的環境在哪裡 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於所有類似網格激發的模式 , 都有相同的對稱軸 , 相同的格子位置 , 在橘色的位置 , 這意味著 , 大腦中所有網格細胞的活動都應該根據這六個方向進行改變 , 或在六個方向之間進行 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振掃描儀 , 讓他們做個電玩遊戲 , 像我給你們看的一樣 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你確實在人類的腦皮層中看到了網格細胞 , 和老鼠的腦部一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車在距離和方向的哪裡 , 可以在他停車的地方延伸建築和邊界 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	可以用邊界偵測細胞的激發來呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園中走出來的路徑 , 在格子細胞激發的路上 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發射 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他所在的位置 , 藉由移動的位置 , 找到最好的位置 , 符合他目前大腦中的位置細胞的發射模式 , 以他停車的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到視覺暗示的位置 , 像他的車到底是不是真的在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許是被綁架了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去拿它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找類似網狀激發的模式 , 我們會在一系列的地點中看到 , 當我們在做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 都會活躍起來 , 比如 , 記得你上次去婚禮的時候 , 例如 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 我們身邊的空間 , 神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重現空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像它們時 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞的相互作用中啟動 , 然後透過這些密集的連結 , 重新啟動邊界細胞 , 來創造你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種我還沒提到的細胞頭向細胞 , 根據你面前的哪種方式 , 它們就像是羅盤 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要創造視覺圖像的視覺方向 , 例如 , 當你在這次婚禮時 , 想像發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代的一個例子 , 其實是在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 例如你如何記憶、想像 , 或甚至是以數十億個獨立的神經元來思考 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾合作驅動的全球安全性 。 這不僅僅是開放式粉絲的遙遠期希望 , 也是納米斯•斯特里迪迪斯的願景 , 納斯托的最高指揮官 , 他在近期的軍事史中共享過的危險時刻 , 來解釋為何未來的安全應該用橋樑建造 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯特瓦里迪斯:納多的最高指揮官如何看待全球安全問題 ?
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我會談到開放資源安全 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須要更安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先回顧二十世紀 , 看看這個安全是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個在法國的戰場 , 位在比利時總部的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過三百天 , 七十萬人被殺 , 每天大約兩千人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你向前推進20世紀的安全性 , 進入第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達林格的戰役 , 300天 , 2百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的戰線轉變成第二次世界大戰的惡性線 , 然後我們進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建造牆壁來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是一座歐洲著名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是德萊納河的橋樑 , ivo和ri奇的小說主題 , 它談到如何在歐洲和巴爾幹半島的一部分 , 長久以來 , 已經有了巨大的牆 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫地 , 聚在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會說 , 開放式安全是要連結國際、國際、私人公共事務 , 並將它與戰略通訊聯繫在一起 , 主要是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這樣做 , 因為我們的全球公有物受到各種不同方式的攻擊 , 而全球公有物的來源都不會受到建築物的威脅 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它的旁邊有康蒂娜電線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是現今世界上非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	盜版在馬拉卡的草地上也很活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它活躍在幾內亞灣 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到了 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	它是全球交通系統中十億美金的不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船 , 500名陸軍陸軍陸戰隊 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海洋 , 網絡海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一張信用卡詐欺 , 把他們淨化超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟的2兆美元不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國內生產總值 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	我們所知的網路海是極為激進的開放最基本的一部分也受到了威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事 , 是販賣所帶來的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片的運動 , 從阿富汗到歐洲的阿富汗到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從安地里北部來的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和販賣 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的損失 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們 , 這是一塊非常高科技的美國海軍裝備 , 用來阻止人口販運 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是由毒品汽車所經營的半合物經營 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它建在南美的叢林裡 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的木筏捕捉到它 , 它帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個組員 , 精密的溝通掃了 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣、毒品、人體、武器、上帝禁止大規模毀滅的武器 , 是對全球公有物的威脅之一 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	咱們現在在阿富汗將它拉在一起 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的popps場 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上80%到90%的糞便、鴉片和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的階段 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的迫切性 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 恐怖主義也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須處理的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 我們現在是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具行不通 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我主張 , 我們不會只從槍枝的桶子中提供安全性 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會只從槍枝的桶子裡提供安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 並且有能力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際、國際化、私人的連結 , 透過網路上策略通訊的概念 , 把彼此拉在一起 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子說明這如何用正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我以為我讀到這個人口統計 , 二十三十多歲的年輕男女 , 在阿富汗大多是文盲 。 」
you would be correct .	你會是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗安全部隊時 , 85%的人看不到 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班早在這些男人和女人的時期就學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們教導他們在識字課程中閱讀 , 由nato和私人企業團體合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們教導了超過二十萬阿富汗安全部隊 , 以基本的層面來閱讀和寫 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你在阿富汗讀和寫時 , 你通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們用很棒的驕傲把筆放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這將國際組織起來 , 有五十個國家參與這項任務 , 國際化 , 這些發展機構和私人公共事務 , 來採取這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也教導他們對抗技能 , 但我認為 , 開放資源安全意味著連結 , 創造出更長的安全效應 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適感 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘姐妹船叫做慈悲 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個 , 舒適的 , 在加勒比海和南美海岸進行病人的治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	一般來說 , 他們會做四十萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	並非由軍隊組成 , 而是由人道主義組織組成:營運希望 , 計畫微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織會派出義工 。
interagency physicians come out .	內部醫師出櫃了 。
they're all part of this .	他們都是這方面的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	給你們舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 跟著他的母親走兩天來到舒適的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他適應時 , 在他的視野中 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , 維埃爾米羅 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	將這個數乘以四十萬名病人的治療 , 這個私人的合作與安全部隊合作 , 你開始以非常不同的角度來看創造安全的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你看到棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能在這張照片中挑出兩位美國軍人士兵嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這兩位小男孩的兩個年輕人 。 這是一系列棒球診所的一部分 , 我們在大聯盟棒球、國家部門 , 他們成立了軍事棒球員 , 他們是真正的士兵 , 但他們參與了這個任務 , 他們在整個南美和加勒比海 , 在全美 , 全美 , 全美 , 和加勒比的巴黎 , 創造了一套外交官 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它向年輕男性和女性表達角色的典範 , 以及關於健身和生活的典範 , 我會說 , 幫助我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這個合作關係的另一個面向是災難救援 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機在2004年海嘯攻擊後 , 殺死了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這些重大災難中 , 海嘯在2004年、25萬人死亡 , 2005年巴基斯坦的kashmiri地震 , 8萬5千人死亡 , 海地地地地震 , 最近發生了三十萬人的地震組合 , 造成日本和核子產業的組合 , 在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到了國際間的合作夥伴 , 和安全的合作關係 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些都是開放資源的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們將它綁在一起 , 漸漸地 , 做像這樣的事 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你看著這個想法: 「 啊 , 行話 , 這些必定是溝通的海道 , 或這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是推特的一張圖 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 , 綠色是地理分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	人口調查是完美的演化 , 世界上六個最大的國家以下降秩序:中國、印度、印度、臉書、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要進入這些蚊帳 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	我們為什麼要參與 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春 , 以及這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉另一個例子 , 就是你如何移動這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦做了這樣的演講 , 前一陣子我跟你們說 , 我在facebook , 朋友我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾笑了一下 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章是ap在電線上運作的 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	在世界上兩個地方被撿起來:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:納多需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	這個故事是個催化劑 , 隔天早上我有數百個臉書朋友請求來自印尼人和芬蘭 , 大多是說: 「 阿米爾 , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 順便說一下 , 納多 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	是的 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們傳遞訊息的方式 , 轉動訊息是我們如何連結國際、國際、私人、以及這些社交網絡 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我按下一個明顯的音符 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一張勇敢英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛中 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在赫爾曼南部 , 在阿富汗南部 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我把他放到這裡來提醒我們 , 我不希望有人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、有能力的軍隊 , 能夠創造出真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	那就是我們是誰的核心 , 我們這麼做 , 來保護言論自由、言論自由 , 所有我們在我們的社會中珍視的事 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道 , 人生不是一場大開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有一支軍隊 , 不論是硬戰 , 還是在巴拉克 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我認為生命是固定的 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須將它撥進去 , 正如我所想 , 我們如何在21世紀創造安全 , 會有時候我們會用真正的戰爭和危機來使用硬實力 , 但還有很多例子 , 如我們今天所說 , 我們的軍隊可以成為21世紀安全、國際安全、私人公共、私人公共、私人溝通的一部分 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我會說我們今天早先聽到維基百科 。 我常用維基百科來查看事實 , 就像在座所有人都很感激 , 維基百科並不是由12位傑出的人鎖在房間寫文章中 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天都有數萬人在輸入信息 , 每天有數百萬人在記錄這些信息 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	對我們所有人而言 , 這是個完美的圖像 , 沒有一個人和所有人一起思考一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有一個人和我們所有人一起思考一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的觀點非常簡單:一個每個人都可以自由地分享所有知識的世界 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 把國際、國際、私人、策略通訊結合在一起 , 在21世紀 , 我們可以創造所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。
